O vos, tres chiers filz, je vos ai acomplit cest livre qui est li derriens de la science de medicine ensamble l’emplissement de lui, et ai fait la fin per ses expositions et par ses declarations.	O you, dear children, I have completed this book which is the last of the medical science together with its contents, and I have made the end through its explanations and by its declarations.
Et m’est venu en vision que je le vos acomplisse avec cest traitier, qui est partie de l’uevre de mains, c’est a savoir «cyrurgie».	And it came to me in vision that I should complete it for you with this treatise, which is part of the work of hands, namely "surgery".
Et por ceu que l’uevre de mains est fortraite en nostre region et est etraingie dou tout en tout, si est perie li science et decopee, et n’est riens demorez de li fuers que les petites descriptions en livres des anciens que les mains ont muees.	And because the work of hands is neglected in our region and completely abandoned everywhere, the science has been lost and fragmented, and nothing remains of its essence except for small descriptions in books by the ancients that have been moved or modified by hand.
Et de ceu est venue li error et li vanitez, et sont closes les ententions et est aloignie li science.	And from this came the errors and vanity, and intentions were closed off and the science was distanced.
Or me semble que je la vuel vivifier ensamble l’ordination de cest traitier selonc la voie d’exposition et de declaration et de l’abreviation;	It seems to me that I should revive it together with the order of this treatise according to the way of exposition and declaration and abbreviation;
et venrai ensamble les formes des ferremens de cautere, et des autres estrumens de l’uevre avec l’ajostement de la declaration et de preparation de li, sicom il est mestier.	and I will come together with the forms of the cautery tools, and of other instruments of the work along with the adjustment of the declaration and preparation of them, as is necessary.
Et por la raison de ceu que nuls boins maistres de mains n’est trovez en nostre tens, est li ars de medicine eslongié.	And because no skilled masters of the craft are found in our time, the art of medicine is neglected.
Et covient celui qui s’en entremet sormonter en la science d’anathomie, si com Galiens dit, tant qu’il saiche la juement des menbres, et les formes et les conjunctions et les separations d’aus, et aient connissance des osses et des nerf et des brais et le nombre d’ous, et le demenement et des voines movans et des reposans, et dou leu de lor issue.	And it is necessary for those who engage in it to excel in the science of anatomy, as Galen says, so that they know the truth about the members, and their forms and conjunctions and separations from each other, and have knowledge of the bones and nerves and sinews and the number of them, and the movement and position of moving and stationary veins, and their points of origin.
Et por ceu dist Ypocras que li nons avec le non est mout, et avec l’uevre est poc;	And for this Hippocrates says that the name with the name is much, and with the work is little;
et meismement en l’art de main.	and especially in the art of practice.
Nos vos disons en l’introite de cest livre que qui n’est conissans des choses devant dites, si se gart qu’il ne chiece en error et qu’il n’ocie les homes;	We tell you at the beginning of this book that whoever is not knowledgeable about the things mentioned above should be careful not to fall into error and harm people;
ensi que j’ai veut maintes fois plusors de ces qui s’entremettent de ceste science et si s’abandonent sen science et sens experiment.	Thus, I have seen many times those who meddle with this science and abandon themselves without knowledge and without experience.
Car je vis un fol mire qui copa I apostume de scrophules ou col d’une femme, et copa les arteres dou col;	For I saw a foolish physician who incised an abscess of scrofula on the neck of a woman, and cut into the arteries of her neck;
por coi tant de sanc issit hors que li femme cheit morte entre ses mains.	for which reason so much blood issued forth that the woman fell dead in his hands.
Et vis I autre mire qui traït une piere d’un home d’eaige, et li piere estoit grans;	And I saw another physician who treated a stone in the urine of a man, and the stone was large;
si emporta avec li une piece de la vessie, et fut mors li hons dedens III jors.	and he took a piece of the bladder with it, and the man died within three days.
Et je i avoie ja esteit apelez por lou traire, et vis la disposition dou malaide et la grandor de la piere, et soi bien s’on lou tailloit il en morroit.	And I had already been called to remove it, and saw the condition of the patient and the size of the stone, and knew well that if they cut into it he would die.
Et vis I autre mire qui prist en cure I duc de nostre terre qui avoit la jambe brisie, et avec la briseure ot plaie;	And I saw another physician who took in charge a duke of our land who had his leg broken, and with the break there was an open wound;
et li mires plains d’ignorance estraint la brisure sus la plaie as esteles par fort lieure, et ne lassa a la plaie point de xalain, et le lassa ensi I termine;	and the physician, full of ignorance, applies the splint too tightly over the wound on the bones, leaving no cloth at all to cover the wound, and he left it thus.
et li comanda qu’il ne la desliast mie;	and he commands that it must not be loosened.
et demora ensi que li jambe fut toute enflee et li piez et vint a perdition.	and he left it like this until the leg and foot were completely swollen, leading to ruin.
Je fuis apelez por venir a lui, et me hastai por venir deslier la jambe;	I was called to come to him, and I hurried to come and loosen the leg;
et quant je l’oi desloie si fut em pais et ne sentit point de dolor.	and when I loosened it, he felt at ease and did not feel any pain.
Mais toute voie li corruptions estoit ja confermee ou membre, et ne la poi saner;	But the corruption was already established in the limb, and it could not be healed.
et ne cessa li corrution d’aler par le membre tant que li membres fut dou tout perdus.	And the corruption continued to spread through the limb until the entire limb was lost.
Et vis I autre mire qui effondra I apostume enchancreit, et puis enflama per le malice de sa signorie.	And I saw another physician who drained the embedded abscess and then inflamed it by the malice of his lordship.
Car chancre, quant il est purs d’umor melancolique, ne covient mie qu’on i(l) touche de fer s’il n’est en teil leu c’on puisse toute oster ce que est corrumpus.	For a carbuncle, when it is full of melancholic humor, must not be touched with iron unless it is in such a place where one can remove all that is corrupted.
Et por ceu, treschier filz, vos est besoig que vos sachiez que oevre de mains est devisee en II divisions:	And for that reason, children, it is necessary that you know that the work of hands is divided into two categories:
c’est asavoir, huevre ou il a peril en plusors dispositions;	that is to say, work where there is danger in many circumstances;
et je mostrerai en chescun leu de cest livre ou il a paour et peril.	and I will show in each place of this book where there is fear and danger.
Por coi il est besoig que vos vos en gardez, si que li fol mire ne puissent mal parler de vos.	Therefore, it is necessary for you to be careful so that the foolish doctor cannot speak ill of you.
Si prenez vos armes en cusenson, et entreprenez vos malaides legierement et fermement, et usez de la millor voie si que per la graice de Deu vos venez a salut et soiez loez;	So take up your arms in this situation, and approach your patients gently yet firmly, and use the best method so that by the grace of God you may reach salvation and be praised;
et lassiez les maladies espoantables de grief saniteit;	and let the dreadful diseases of severe illness be left;
et ostez vos armes de ceu que vos fait douter, et aiez foit en vos si que vos puissiez venir de cestui monde a l’autre de gloire.	and remove yourselves from what causes doubt, and act in such a way that you may come from this world to the next in glory.
Galiens dist en aucuns de ses amonestemens:	Galenus said in some of his admonitions:
«Ne prenez mie en cure male maladie, que vos ne soiez apelez fol mire.	Do not take care of a bad illness, or you may be called a mad doctor.
» J’ai deviseit cest traitier selonc III chapitres.	I have devised this treatise according to three chapters.
Li premiers chapitres est des cauteres de feu et dé cauteres de medicine ague, et est li chapitres ordenez de lou chief jusques as piez;	The first chapter is about fire cauterizations and medicinal hot cauterizations, and the chapter is organized from head to feet;
et des formes des estrumens, et des ferremens de cautere, et de tout ceu qui est necessaire en l’ueuvre.	and about the forms of instruments, and cauterization tools, and all that is necessary for the work.
Li secons chapitres si est de taillier et de percier, et des ventouses et des plaies, et des estractions des saiettes, et des semblans choses;	The second chapter is about cutting and piercing, and cupping and wounds, and the extraction of arrows, and similar things;
et est li chapitres ordenez et les formes des estrumens.	and the chapter is organized and the forms of the instruments.
Li tiers chapitres est de restorer les dislocations et des torcions, et des semblans choses;	The third chapter is about restoring dislocations and twists, and similar things;
et est ordeneiz des lou chief jusc’as piez, et des formes des estrumens.	and is organized from the head to the feet, and the forms of the instruments.
Ainsois que nos nos remembriens de l’uevre, il covient que je die la qualiteit de l’aide et dou nuisement de chescune complexion.	Thus, as we remember the work, it is necessary for me to tell about the quality of the aid and harm of each temperament.
Je dis que li qualiteis de l’aide, et dou nuisement, est li plus longe parole et subtilz science et li secrez reponus;	I say that the qualities of help and harm are the longest discourse and subtle science and secret responses;
et de ceu parlerent li plusors des saiges, et s’acorderent a ceu;	and many wise people spoke about this, and agreed on it;
et me soffisent poc lor paroles, car je redous la longesce.	And they bore my patience with their words, for I fear the length.
Je dis que cautere aide universement a toute complexion ou il a matiere, fuer que II complexions:	I say that the cautery universally aids all temperaments where there is matter, except for two temperaments:
c’est a savoir complexion chaude sens matere, et complexion seche sens matere.	that is to say, the hot temperament without matter, and the dry temperament without matter.
En complexion chaude et seche ensamble matiere, deviserent aucun et dirent que cautere i est grans aide;	In the hot and dry temperament together with matter, some have discussed and said that cautery is great help there;
et li autre dirent le contraire:	and others said the opposite:
que cautere ne vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de sechour.	that cautery is not useful for a disease that comes from heat and dryness.
Car li nature dou feu si est chaude, et ne doit mie estre cureiz de chaude maladie par chalor, ne per sechour;	For the nature of fire is hot, and it should not be used to treat a hot disease by heat, nor for dryness;
et dist cil qui dist lou contraire que cautere fait grant aide a maladie chaude et seche que vient en cors des homes.	And he who says the opposite that the cautery greatly helps the hot and dry disease that comes to the bodies of men.
Car quant tu comperes le cors de l’ome et sa moistor a la complexion dou feu, tu trueves le cors froit.	For when you examine the body of the man and his moisture according to the complexion of fire, you find the body cold.
Et je m’acorde a ceste parole.	And I agree with this statement.
Car je l’ai troveit aucune fois per experiment.	For I have found it to be true on some occasions through experience.
Et toute voie, ne s’en entremette mie fuers que cil qui l’a esproveit, et qui conoit par lonc usaige le chapistre des cauteres, et la diversiteit des complexions des homes, et les dispositions et les causes de lor maladies, et les sorvenues et l’espaice dou tens;	And in every way, do not intervene except for he who has experienced it, and who knows through long use the chapter of cauteries, and the diversity of human constitutions, and the predispositions and causes of their diseases, and the outcomes and the space of time;
des autres complexions n’avons nos mie paour, meismement em maladies froides et moistes.	we do not fear other constitutions, especially in cold and moist diseases.
Et tuit li mire s’asemblerent et s’acorderent au cautere.	And all the doctors assembled and agreed on the cauterization.
Et sachiez, filz, que cautere ensamble feu si est des secrez des cures, et de plus grant bonteit que cautere de medicine ardant.	And know, son, that the fire cautery together is of the secrets of cures, and of greater goodness than the burning medicinal cautery.
Car li feus est simples, et ne vient mie fuers que au membre qui est cuis, et ne nuit a autre membre se poc nom.	For the fire is simple, and does not affect any part other than the limb that is being treated, and it does no harm to another member if one can name such.
Les medicines ardans vienent de membre a autre en aloignant, et font venir au membre maladies de grief sanation;	The hot medicines come from one member to another in succession, and cause the member to become ill with difficult recovery;
et par aventure ocit lou malaide.	and by chance kill the patient.
Li feus por sa hautece et por la bonteit de sa substance ne fait mie ceu, s’il n’i a superfluiteit.	The fire, for its height and for the quality of its substance, does not cause that, if there is no excess.
Et ceu vos ai je troveit par experiment et par la longesce dou servise et de l’estude que j’ai mis en l’art, et esteit sus la verteit des choses;	And this I have found through experience and by the length of service and study that I have dedicated to the art, and it is upon the truth of things;
et por ceu je m’escuse de la longesce de la parole, car il ne me plait mie que je vos oste le secreit qui est reponus ou feu, et la qualiteit de l’uevre, coment il deboute les maladies des cors, si com li philosophe le dit en demostrant;	and for this reason I excuse myself for the length of speech, because it does not please me to take from you the secret that is hidden in the fire, and the quality of the work, how it overcomes bodily diseases, as the philosopher says in demonstrating;
or le recevez en vos pensees.	therefore receive it in your thoughts.
Et sachiez, fil, que il s’acorderent en quel tens doient estre faites les cauteres, et eslirent prientens.	And know, son, that they agreed on what time should be chosen for performing the cauterizations, and selected appropriate times.
Et je dis que cautere est covenable en tous tens, por ceu que li nuisemens sorvenans est desoz mis par l’aide dou cautere;	And I say that the cautery is appropriate at all times, because the evils arising are removed by the aid of the cautery;
et meismement se li cauteres est por dolors necessaires fors et hastans que ne puent atendre le tens que plus grans malice ne veigne au membre.	and especially if the cauterizations are necessary for pains that cannot wait, so that the time does not allow greater harm to come to the member.
Et n’i pensez onques, chier fil, si com font li fol mire;	And think nothing of it, dear child, as foolish doctors do;
car a la maladie qui est sanee par cautere n’a point de revenue;	for the disease that is cured by cauterization has no return;
et il le dient ensi;	and they say it thus;
mais il n’est mie si com il cuident, por ce que cauteres nen est que medicine qui mue la complexion, et seche les humors que sont cause de la dolor, et vaut mues que medicine por le hastement de sa valor, et por la vertut de son oevre et de sa signorie.	but it is not as they believe, because cauterizations are a medicine that changes the complexion, and dries up the humors which are the cause of the pain, and is worth more than medicine for its haste in healing due to its power, and the virtue of its work and sovereignty.
Et possans chose est que li maladie viegne aucune fois selonc la complexion dou malaide et lou leu de la maladie et sa vertut;	And it is possible for the illness to come sometimes according to the constitution of the patient and the location of the illness and its power;
et sont assemblees en lui les superfluitez par l’aquisition des viandes et des semblans choses, se ce n’est cauteres administrez em leu ou il ait poc de superfluitez et de moistor, si com cauteres de dens por la dolor, et les semblans choses, et teil dolor ne revient mie;	and are gathered within him the excesses through the acquisition of foods and similar things, unless cauterizations are administered in places where there is an abundance of excesses and moisture, such as cauterizations for toothache pain, and similar things, and such pain does not return;
mais ce avient poc.	but it rarely happens.
Et mout de gens n’entendent mie por coi cauteres est apelez li derriens de medecine, et c’est voir;	And many people do not understand why cauterizations are called the rear of medicine, and this is true;
mais il ne croient mie que cauteres vaille aprés medicine, mais lor ententions est fause, et est cauteres li derriens de medicine por ceu que quant nos aministrons manieres de cures en aucune maladie et elles ne valent, adonc administrons nos le cautere, et il vaut.	but they do not believe that cauterizations are worth after medicines, but their beliefs are false, and cauterizations are the rear of medicine because when we administer methods of treatment in certain illnesses and they are ineffective, then we administer the cauterization, and it works.
Adonques apert bien que cauteres est li derriens de medicine, ne mie selonc l’entention des folz mires.	Then it is clear that cauterization is among the last of medicines, not as the foolish doctors intend.
Li ancien dirent que cauteres d’estrument d’or est muedres que de fer, et ne dirent ceu fuers que por la qualiteit de l’or et por la hautece de sa substance;	The ancients said that cauterizations with an instrument of gold are milder than those of iron, and they said this not for any reason other than the quality of the gold and the height of its substance;
et dirent que li leus de cautere ne fait mie porriture, mais ceu n’est mie voir car je l’ai esprovei, et ai troveit que c’est voir en aucuns homes;	and they said that the scar from a cauterization does not cause irritation, but this is not true because I have tested it and found that it is true in some people;
et cauteres d’or vaut mues que de fer, si com il lou dirent.	and cauterizations with gold are gentler than those with iron, as they claim.
Et toutevoie quant tu chaufes estrument d’or, tu ne seis mie quant il est chaus par la color de l’or, et s’est tantost refroidiez;	And still, when you heat an instrument of gold, you cannot tell by its color when it is hot, and it cools down so quickly;
et s’on le chaufe trop;	and if you heat it too much;
si font au feu;	do with fire;
et ensi i a assez d’empechement.	and thus there is sufficient obstruction.
Et por ce usons nos de cautere de feir que nos l’avons mues apparilliet a nostre oevre.	And for this reason, we use fire cautery which we have prepared for our work.
Or vos ai ordeneit cest chapitre des lou chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que li voie soit plus legiere a trover.	I have ordered this chapter from head to foot, so that the way may be easier to find.
dou cautere olivaire	of the olive cauterization
Cist cauteres vaut a moistor et a froidor sus lou cerveil, et en i a dous c’on fait par la cause d’une maladie qui est apelee «soda», et par la cause de maintes humors qui dessendent dou chief as eulz, et as oreilles, et por multitude de songes et dolor de dens et dolor de gorge, et meismement a toutes maladies qui vienent de froidor si com paralisie et sode et apoplexie et semblans maladies.	This cautery is useful for moisture and cold affecting the brain, and there are two that are made due to a disease called "soda," and due to many humors descending from the head to the eyes, and ears, and for an abundance of dreams and pain in the teeth and throat, and especially for all diseases caused by cold such as paralysis, soda, apoplexy, and similar illnesses.
Li forme de cest cautere si est que li malaides soit espurgiez par medicine solutive mondifiant le chief III nuis ou IIII, selonc ceu que li vertus et li eaige et li acostumance dou malaide le puet soffrir;	The form of this cautery is such that the patient should be purged by a solvent medicine cleansing the head for three nights or four, according to what the virtues and age and habit of the patient can endure;
et puis fai rere lou chief dou malaide.	and then do behind the head of the patient.
Et puis le fai seoir croisiet entre tes mains, et mettre ses mains sor som peis;	And then have him sit cross-legged between your hands, and place his hands on his thighs;
aprés met la racine de ta palme sus la racine de son neis entre ses II eulz;	then place the root of your palm on the base of his nose between his two eyes;
et lai ou venra tes dois moiens, si saigne d’enche puis eschaufe le cautere qui est apelé «olivare», de coi ci est li forme:	And there where your two means will come, if it bleeds then heat the cautery which is called "olivare", of which here is the form:
Et le met sor le leu signiet d’encre, et fai en dessendant et en estraignant ta main poc et poc en trestornant;	And place on the spot an ink stain, and do it descending and pulling your hand little by little in turning;
puis lieve ta main isnelement, et rewarde le leu se tu vois l’os I sol petit;	then lift your hand gently, and examine the spot if you see the bone slightly;
et se tu ne lou vois, si rencomence le cautere tant que tu voies l’os si com je lou t’ai dit;	and if you do not see it, then repeat the cautery until you see the bone as I have told you;
aprés pren I poc de seil, et met en awe et molle coton dedens, et met sor le leu, et li laisse III jors;	after take a little wax, and place soft cotton inside it, and put it on the spot, and leave it for three days;
aprés met sus cotun moilliet en burre;	Then put moist wool over it;
et laisse sus tant que li eschaudure soit ostee;	and leave it on until the burn is gone;
aprés cure la plaie de l’oignement qui est apelez «tetrafarmaçon», tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then treat the wound with an ointment called "tetrafarmakon" until it is healed.
Et se dirent li ancien, que quant plus demoure overte li plaie, plus s’espurge;	And the ancient ones said that the longer the wound remains open, the more it purges;
et por ce si aide mues.	and for this reason, it aids in healing.
Et dirent aucun de ces que on doit tant lassier le cautere que partie de l’os soit arse, et puis rese on ceu qui est ars de l’os, et soit curez.	And some say that one should leave the cautery long enough for part of the bone to be burned, and then remove what is burned from the bone, and treat it.
Et dient li autre c’on doit le cautere tant lassier sus, et bouter si fort c’on abaite de l’os ausi large comme I vertoil que les femmes mettent en lor fusez por ceu que les humors issent mues hors;	And others say that the cautery should be left on for so long and pressed so hard that it penetrates the bone as wide as the rod that women put in their hair to draw out the humors;
et doit on lassier la plaie longement overte;	and one must leave the wound open for a long time;
aprés le doit on curer et sodeir.	after which it should be cleaned and treated.
Et ces II manieres de cauteres ne me semblent mie estre bones dou tout en tout, fuers qu’en aucuns homes ou il ait voie de paor;	And these two methods of cauterization do not seem entirely good to me, except in some people where there is reason for fear;
et mues me semble que je lou doie laissier;	and I think that I should leave it out;
car li chiés li est afoiblis par les solutions continuees de nature, si com nos le tesmoignons ens autres membres;	for the head is weakened by continuous natural solutions, as we witness in other limbs;
et meisme quant li chiés dou malaide est foibles par nature, et li premiere semblance de cautere est plus salve et muedre por moi, et de celi use je oevre en donques emsamble salut.	and even when the head of the patient is weak by nature, and the first appearance of cauterization seems safer and more appropriate to me, I then proceed with it for safety.
de l’anciainne dolor dou chief	of the old pain of the head
Quant en tout le chief vient dolor croniques, et dure longement, si doit user li malaides yeris et pilules qui sont apelees «cochie», et d’espurgement de chief et d’oiles et d’emplastres;	When chronic pain comes to the entire head and lasts for a long time, the patient should use herbs and pills which are called "cochie", and undergo purging of the head and oils and plasters;
et s’on li fait le cautere que nos avons devant dit, et il ne vaut.	and if one performs the cautery that we mentioned before, it is not effective.
Pren warde se li chiés dou malade est de fort nature, et qu’il ne soit trop froit;	Take care if the head of the patient is of strong constitution, and that it is not too cold;
adonques le cauterize desoz celui cautere un poc que nos avons dit desus.	then cauterize slightly below that point as we mentioned above.
Aprés fai cautere sus chescune corne dou chief jusc’a l’os, si com devant avons dit, et fai I cautere ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz»;	After perform cauterization on each horn of the head up to the bone, as we said before, and perform the cauterization at the place called "vasselz";
et est I leus en coi on met ventouses;	and there are the places where one applies suction cups;
et alige ta main si que tu ne voises mie jusc’a l’os:	and place your hand so that you do not see the bone:
li malaides sent trop plus grant dolor en cest cautere que as autres, et je em parlerai aillors;	the patient feels much greater pain in this cautery than in others, and I will speak of it later;
et covient que li cauteres des cornes soient plus subtis que cil dont on cautere la moieneteit dou chief, et c’est li forme:	and it is necessary that the cauteries for the horns be finer than those used to cauterize the soft part of the head, and this is their form:
dou cautere dou chief	For the cautery of the head
Quant en une partie dou chief vient dolor sodaine, et est estendue li maladie jusc’a l’oil, et li chiés est espurgiez par medicines mondifians, et on a fait les autres cures que j’ai dit en la division des maladies, et tout ceu ne profite mie:	When sudden pain comes to one part of the head, and the illness extends to the eye, and the joint is purged by cleansing medicines, and all the other treatments that I have mentioned in the division of diseases have been performed, and none of this helps:
adonques li fai cauteres selonc II manieres, c’est a savoir de medicine ague et de feir.	Then I perform cauterizations according to two methods, namely with dry medicine and with fire.
Li cauteres de medicine ague si est que tu preignes une doce d’alz, et oste l’escorce et le recope I poc as II chiés, et puis fent la temple ou li dolor tient en teil maniere que tu puisses reponre la doce d’alz desoz le cuir;	The cauterization with dry medicine is done by taking a piece of alum, removing the skin and wrapping it in a small cloth, then applying it to the temple where the pain is located so that you can place the wrapped piece of alum beneath the skin.
et quant elle sera reponuee si le lie et l’estraint bien et le laisse ensi XII houres;	and when it is placed, cover and press it well and leave it for twelve hours;
et puis le deslie et trait fuers la doce d’ail, et laisse la plaie ensi II jors ou III;	and then remove it and treat the area with garlic wrapped in cloth, and leave the wound like this for two or three days;
puis met sus cotun plongiet en burre tant que porreture en isse.	then apply a poultice of butter wrapped in cloth until it saturates the area.
Aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez;	After the treatment of ointment until it is healed;
et se tu vues si fai ceu d’aucunes medicines comburans que j’ai escrites ou dozime traitier des medicines comburans.	and if you wish to do so, use some burning medicines that I have written in the twelfth chapter on burning medicines.
Li cautere de fer si est selonc ceste meniere.	The cautery of iron is done according to this method.
Chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	Heat the cautery which has the following form:
Et est apelez «clos» por ceu que li chief est fait a la forme d’un clo ou il ait I poc de corbeure, et em mileu a une petite apparance;	And it is called "clos" because the head is shaped like a dome with a small depression in the middle.
et le met sor le leu dolorous, et tien ta main et trestorne le feir un poc legierement, tant que li moitiez de l’espés dou keur soit arse;	and place it on the painful area, and hold your hand and turn the fire slightly, until half of the thickness of the heart's surface is burned.
et lieve ta main que li artere n’arde, que est defuers, et decorre habundance de sanc.	and lift your hand so that the artery does not burn, which is outside, and to avoid excessive bleeding.
Aprés met coton en awe de seil, et met sor le leu par III jors;	After place cotton on bandage for three days;
puis i met coton moilliet em burre, et puis cure le leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez;	then place moistened cotton on leather, and then treat the wound with ointment until it is healed;
et se tu vuelz cauterize ceste emigraine avec le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare», a tout la pointe, et te garde de coper l’artere en ceste emigraine qui n’est mie anciaine.	and if you wish to cauterize this swelling with the cautery called "cultellare", do it to the entire tip, and be careful not to cut the artery in this swelling which is not old.
de emigraine	of swelling/inflammation
Quant tu cures emigraine si com nos avons devant dit en divisions des maladies, et ne profite mie, et vois que li cauteres devant dis de la medicine et dou fer ne li soffit mie, adonques covient il que tu eschaufes le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare» tant qu’il soit blans;	When you treat a swelling as we have said before in the division of diseases, and it does not improve, and see that the cauterizations previously mentioned from medicine and iron do not help, then you must heat the cautery called "cultellare" until it is white;
et seigne ainsois sor le leu doillant une ligne de demi doi de lonc, et oste ta main une fois, et l’estrain que tu ne coper l’artere et que ne viegnes jusc’a l’os;	and mark thus on the painful area a line half a digit long, and remove your hand once, to avoid cutting the artery and reaching the bone;
et te warde de la mandibule que muet quant on menjut, et li ners n’ait regart que la muet et que spasmus ne veigne a malaide, et te warde de decorrement de sanc de l’artere quant elle sera copee, ou copement ait grant paour et meismement a celui que ne s’i conoit, et qui n’est estudians et esprovez;	and be wary of the mandible that moves when eating, and the nerve must be careful so that it does not cause movement and spasm in the patient, and beware of blood loss from the artery when it is cut, as cutting causes great fear and especially for one who is not familiar with it, and who is not a student and experienced;
et laisse l’uevre em mi voie;	and leave the work midway;
mais je vos dirai coment on restainche sanc quant li artere est copee, et je vos mostrerai a leu ou il afiert en cest livre.	but I will tell you how to control bleeding when the artery is cut, and I will show you where it appears in this book.
Et se tu vois que cist cauteres ne soffise mie a la maladie, et li malaides est soffrans, cauterize le enmi le chief ausi com nos avons dit, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee;	And if you see that these cauterizations do not alleviate the disease, and the patient is suffering, cauterize on top of the head as we have said, and treat the wound until it is healed;
et se tu vues, aministre le cautere que nos avons dit ou chapistre de l’estraction de l’artere, avec le cautere qui ait II coutelz;	and if you see it necessary, apply the cauterization that we mentioned in the chapter on the extraction of the artery, using a cauterizing instrument with two blades;
et est cist cauteres millors de celui et plus aidans.	and this type of cauterization is better and more beneficial.
de la dolor des oreilles de part froidor	of the pain in the ears due to coldness
Quant en l’oreille vient dolor de froit, et on i a ovreit de medicines solutives et des autres cures que nos avons dit en la division, et li dolors ne se muet, adonques eschaufe cest cautere qui est apelez «poins», de coi ci est li forme:	When pain from coldness comes to the ear, and medicine has been applied and other treatments we have described in the division are used, but the pain does not subside, then heat this cautery called "points," here is its form:
Aprés pointoie tout entor l’oreille malaide, ou entor les II se la dolor tient en ambedous, et t’esloigne un poc ensus de la racine de l’oreille puis que tu as signiet le leu d’enche;	After puncture all around the diseased ear, or both ears if the pain is in both, and move up a little from the base of the ear after you have marked the spot;
et ait X poins entor chescune oreille;	and place ten points around each ear;
aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	after treating the area until it is healed.
de la torture de la bouche	of the treatment of the mouth
Torture qui doit estre curee par cautere nen est fuers que de celles que muevent de fleume, si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladie;	A condition that must be treated with cauterization is not exempt from those that move due to phlegm, as we have said in the division of diseases;
et ne faire point de cautere as semblances que vienent de sechor et de spame de ners.	and do not perform cauterization on conditions that come from dryness and nerve spasms.
Quant tu cures ceste semblance de torture qui muet de fleume d’ydres et d’espurgemens de chief et de gargarisme, et ceu ne vaut, adonc covient que tu cauterizes le malaide de III cauteres:	When you treat this condition of pain that moves due to phlegm from the head and gargling, and if it does not improve, then you must cauterize the patient with three cauterizations:
l’une en la racine de l’oreille, et l’autre un poc defuers la temple, et le tier en l’ajostement des II levres;	one at the root of the ear, and the other a little outside the temple, and the third at the junction of the two lips;
et met le cautere en la partie qui apert saine, et li fai cautere endroit le chief de l’oreille desus un poc desoz la corne dou chief, et un autre en la temple ausi longe com uns poce;	and place the cautery on the part that appears healthy, and apply it towards the top of the ear just below the point of the ear, and another in the temple as far as a palm's length;
et laisse le cautere tant sus que li moitiez dou keur soit arse;	and leave the cautery on until half of the heart area is burned;
et c’est li forme dou cautere:	and this is the form of the cautery:
Et est li semblance dou cutellaire que nos avons mise devant, mais il est un poc plus subtilz et covient que li coutelz soit un poc plus gros;	And it is similar to the cautery we have described before, but it is a bit more subtle and the knife should be slightly larger;
aprés cure lou leu si com j’ai devant dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	After treating the area as I have said before, until it is healed.
Quant apoplexie est ancieinne et tu la cures ensi com nos avons dit, et il ne profite mie, et li malaides n’ait fievre, adonques li fai IIII cauteres:	When apoplexy is long-standing and treating it as we have described does not help, and the patient has no fever, then you perform four cauterizations:
II sus les II cornes dou chief, et I emmi le chief, et I ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz» si com nos avons devant dit, et lou derrien cautere sus la bouche de l’estomac;	Two on the two horns of the head, one in the middle of the head, and one at the place called "vasselz" as we have said before, and the last cauterization above the stomach.
et soit curez si com nos avons dit devant.	and let them be treated as we have said before.
de litargie	For litargia
A cest maladie covient doner au malaide yeres grans et pilules mondifians le cerveil;	For this illness, it is necessary to give the patient large doses of medicine and pills to purify the brain;
aprés reis lou chief dou malaide tout, et li met sus l’occipite l’emplaustre de sinapi qui est escrit ou traitier des emplastres;	After raising the head of the patient completely, place the plaster of mustard, which is written in the treatise on plasters, upon the occiput;
et c’est li maniere dou cautere:	and this is the method of the cautery:
si lou fai si com j’ai dit.	do as I have said.
S’il est sanez ensi, boin est;	If it is done thus, it is good;
et s’il ne l’est, se li fai III cauteres des emmi le chief en dessendant jusc’a col, et ait d’espaice entre chescun cautere I doi de gros;	and if it is not, make three cauterizations from the middle of the head descending to the neck, and let there be a space of one thumb's width between each cauterization;
et le cure si com les autres, et se tu i vues ajoster, et li malaides est soffrans, se li fai I cautere en mileu;	and treat it as you would the others, and if you wish to add more, and the patient is suffering, make one cauterization in the middle;
et se mestiers est, II autres sus les II cornes, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	and if necessary, two others on the two horns, and treat until it is healed;
et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare», si com j’ai devant dit.	and let the cauterization be what is called "olivare," as I said before.
de la froidor dou chief	of the coldness of the head
Il covient que li chief soit mundifiez de yeres et de ceu que nos avons devant dit;	It is necessary that the head be cleansed of hair and of what we said before;
aprés reis le chief dou malaide, puis li fai cautere emmi le chief et sus chescune corne, et I derrier et III sus l’espinee dou col;	after raising the head of the patient, then perform cauterization in the middle of the head and on each horn, and one behind and three along the spine of the neck;
et se tu en as plus mestier, et li cors est moiste et li malaides est soffrans, et li maladie est fors, se li fai IIII cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos;	and if you need more, and the body is moist and the patient is suffering, and the illness is severe, then perform four cauterizations along the spine of the back;
et li laisse tant que li plus dou keur soit ars, et lieve ta main;	and leave it until the most reddened part is burned, and lift your hand;
aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare» que nos avons devant dit.	after the treatment until it is healed, and use the cauterization method called "olivare" which we mentioned earlier.
de l’epilempsie	of epilepsy
Li epilentiques ne doit useir de cautere fuers que cil qui est fleumatique, et covient premier mondifier le cerveil de yeres et d’autres cures que nos avons dites en la division quant li malaides est grans et soffrans de penre medicine.	Those with epilepsy should not use the fire cautery except for those who are phlegmatic, and it is necessary first to modify the brain from herbs and other treatments that we have mentioned in the section when the patient is large and suffers greatly from severe illness.
Et se c’est uns enfes qui ne lou puisse soffrir, se li fai gargarisme et mastication mondifiant le cerveil sovent avec bones viandes;	And if it is a child who cannot bear it, perform gargling and chewing remedies to cleanse the brain often with good meats;
aprés li reis lou chief em mileu, et i fai I cautere selonc ce que nos avons dit devant, et I cautere sus lou vassel, et sus chescune corne;	after placing the head in the middle, perform the cauterization as we said before, and do the cauterization on the vessel, and on each horn;
et se li malaides est fors et soffrans, se li fai cauteres si com j’ai dit a celui qui ait paralisie et mollification de cors, sus l’espinee dou dos et dou col, et soit li cauteres olivier selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	and if the patient is outside and suffering, perform cauterizations as I said for those who have paralysis and weakness of the body, on the spine of the back and neck, and use olive cauterizations as described.
Se li malaides est enfes, se li fai I cautere subtil selonc ceste maniere:	If the patient is a child, perform the subtle cautery according to this method:
Quant par la cause de melancolie sunt les superfluitez ou les moistors corrumpues et fleume grosse, adonques lou cauterize de teils cauteres com nos avons dit a celui qui ait paralisie.	When due to melancholy the excesses or moistures are corrupted and phlegm is thick, then apply such cauterizations as we have described to one who suffers from paralysis.
Et se par la cause de melancolie est li superfluitez declinans a melancolie, et est li cors dou malaide moistes, adonc li done a boivre chose par coi li cervelz soit mundifiez, selonc ceu qu’il est devant en la division.	And if due to melancholy the excesses tend towards melancholy and the patient's body is moist, then give them something to drink that purifies the brain according to what is stated earlier in the division.
Aprés reis lou chief dou malaide;	After raising the patient's head;
aprés fai I torteil de lin bien fait, ausi com I cercle, si le met emmi le chief;	after making the bandage of linen well, as circular, place it on the head;
et li malaides sié croisiez, et soit bien tenus de toutes pars;	and the patient should sit crossed-legged, held firmly from all sides;
aprés presente le linement, et vaut mues de burre de berbis ancien;	then present the linting material, which should be wool from an old sheep;
et lou chaufe a feu tempreement, si que li dois s’on li boute le puisse soffrir;	and heat it over the fire until it can be applied to the patient’s wound without causing pain;
aprés vuide le cercle par dedens emmi le chief, et lou laisse refroidier;	then empty the circle inside the head bandage and let it cool;
et fai ce a malaide chescune semaine une fois avec autre governement boin, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and do this for the patient once every week with other good management until he is healed.
Ou se tu vues cauterize lou en faisant poins plusors a tot le cautere.	When you wish to cauterize it, make multiple punctures all over the cauterized area.
Ceste maniere de cautere amoistit le cerveil igaument;	This method of cautery moistens the brain excessively;
et puis met sus coton moilliet en burre et en graisse de geline.	and then apply cotton soaked in butter and goose fat.
de l’awe des eulz	from the pain of the eyes
Quant awe vient premierement as eulz par les signes que j’ai dit en la division, adonques encomence et done boivre au malaide chose mundifiant le chief, et le warde de toutes moistors, et lou fai suer ou bain plusors fois a jeun.	When the pain first comes to the eyes by the signs I have mentioned in the division, then begin and give the patient something purifying to drink, and protect them from all moisture, and make them sweat in baths several times on an empty stomach.
Aprés li comande a rere son chief, et li fai cautere emmi le chief, et li fai II cauteres sus les II temples se li dessendemens de l’awe est as II eulz ensamble, ou en I se li dessendemens est en I;	After instructing him to lie with his head down, perform a cautery in the middle of the head, and apply two cauterizations on each temple if the descent of the brain is to both eyes together, or one if it is to one eye;
et cope a tout le cautere toutes les voines et les arteres que sont desoz le keur, et soient li cautere lonc selon lou large de la temple;	and cover the entire cautery with all the veins and arteries that are below the heart, and let the cautery be long according to the width of the temple;
et te warde de decorrement de sanc, et se tu vois trop de sanc issir, si li estainche de teil pooir com tu as.	and be wary of excessive bleeding, and if you see too much blood coming out, stop it with as much force as you have.
Et je t’enseignerai en l’estraction des arteres et a l’incision la cautele coment tu l’estencheras;	And I will teach you in the extraction of arteries and in the incision the caution how you will stop it;
et aucune fois fait on cautere ou hatereil desoz les II os derrier.	and sometimes a cautery is made to separate the two bones behind.
dou cors des larmes	from the body of tears
Quant les larmes des eulz sont ancienes et acostumees et sont sus les voines, ou delez les arteres que sont en l’aparance dou chief defors;	When the tears from the eyes are old and habitual and are on the veins, then separate the arteries that appear on the head outside;
et on voit que c’est des superfluitez froides fleumatiques, adonques li fai le cautere que j’ai dit en l’encomencement de l’awe dessendant as eulz:	and when you see that it is due to cold phlegmatic excesses, then I make the cautery that I mentioned at the beginning of the chapter descending to the eyes:
I cautere emmi le chief, et II cauteres sus les II temples, et II cauteres ou haiterel desoz les II os;	I make one cautery in the middle of the head, and two cauteries on the two temples, and two cauteries where the two bones are separated;
et s’il i a besoigne plus, si le cauterize saigement desus le sorcil a tout I petit cautere.	and if there is need for more, then cauterize carefully above the eyebrow with the small cautery.
dou cors des larmes par dedens les eulz	from the body tears within the eyes
Quant tu le medicines selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et il ne profite mie, adonques done a boivre a malaide III nuis cochies;	When you treat him according to what we have said in the division, and it is of no use, then give the patient three cups to drink for three nights;
aprés li reis le chief, et li fai cautere ou mileu dou cautere olivaire;	after the king's head, and apply the cauterization in the middle of the olive-shaped cautery;
et fai II cauteres dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis» sus les II sorcis, un poc desoz les chevous;	and make two cauterizations of the cautery called "clavilis" on the two eyebrows, a little below the hair;
et te warde de l’artere que tu ne la coper.	and be careful of the artery so that you do not cut it.
Et c’est li forme dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis»:	And this is the shape of the cautery called "clavilis":
Quant li papiere de l’oil est mollifie de maladie et de moistor, adonques la cautarize de cest cautere qui est apelez «olivare».	When the white of the eye becomes softened due to illness and moisture, then cauterize it with this cautery called "olivare".
de coi ci est li forme:	Of which this is the form:
Et se tu vues si fai II cauteres sus les II sorcis ausi lons com li sorcilz sont;	And if you wish, make two cauterizations on the two eyebrows as long as the eyebrows are;
et n’i lassiez mie la main fors que tant que li tierce partie de la papiere soit arse, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	and do not let go of the hand until a third part of the paper is burned, according to the manner I have said.
dou poil qui point l’oil	of the hair that points towards the eye
Aucune fois avient que li poil des oilz sont convertit au pardedens, et poignent l’oil, et i fait on cauteres selonc II manieres:	Sometimes the hair of the eyes grows inward and pricks the eye, and one makes cauterizations according to two methods:
c’est a savoir de feu, ou de medicine ardant.	that is to say, with fire, or with burning medicine.
Ou cautere de feu comande au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient lons et igals;	For the fire cautery, instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even;
et s’il le poignent a lor nassance, se li estraint les eulz qu’il ne se muevent tant qu’il naissent.	and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Quant il naissent et i sont igalz, adonques met le malaide en ton sain;	When they grow and are even, then place the patient in your care;
aprés seigne sus la papiere des eulz une figure que soit ausi com li fuelle dou mirte, et soit li comencemens dou signe delez les poilz;	after marking on the paper around the eyes a shape that is like the leaf of myrtle, and let the beginning of the mark be near the hairs;
puis i met coton moilliet en glaire d’uef et muscillaige de persillion sus l’oil, puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	then place cotton moistened in egg white and parsley juice on the eye, then heat the cautery which is of this form:
Aprés cauterize sus la figure que tu as signiet poc et poc mout de fois, que li keurs soit ars lai endroit;	After cauterizing around the shape that you marked little by little many times, so that the flesh is burned in that place;
et li signes de la santeit de l’uevre est que tu voies la papiere retraite, et les poilz levez a la pointure de l’oil;	and the signs of the treatment's success are that you see the paper retracting, and the hairs raised at the edge of the eye;
adonques lieve ta main, et laisse ensi III jors, puis i met coton moilliet en burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee;	then lift your hand, and leave it like this for three days, then place moistened cotton with butter until the inflammation subsides;
aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	after the treatment of salving until it is healed.
Et se aprés ceu vienent li poilz, et li papiere est mollifie adonques rencomence le cautere sus cel leu meisme, si com tu as fait premiers;	And if the hairs come after that, and the skin is softened, then restart the cautery on the same spot as you did before;
et se li poil sont defuer, si le cauterize tant que li papiere soit levee a son leu natureil, et soit igals, et ne poignent mie li poil l’oil.	and if the hairs are absent, then cauterize until the skin rises to its natural position and is even, so that the hairs do not prick the eye.
Li cauteres de medicine ardant est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient grans et igalz, puis fai de parchemin la forme de la foille de mirte;	The fiery cauterization is that you instruct the patient to let the hairs grow until they are large and even, then make a form from parchment in the shape of a myrtle leaf;
puis pren de savon fransois et de vive chalz, de chescun une .З., et broie ensamble bien;	then take one part each of French soap and live charcoal, and grind them together well;
et le fai hastanment, si qu’il ne refroide, puis en espant sus la forme que tu es fait sicom la foille dou mirte, et met sus la papiere des eulz;	And I do it quickly so that it does not cool, then spread it over the area as you would with myrtle leaves, and place a paper on the eyes;
et se li maladie tient en I oil soulement, si doit on ovrer en I, et se en ambedous ausi;	And if the illness affects only one eye, then treat that one, and both if it is in both;
et met desoz l’oil coton moilliet en abin d’uef;	And place cotton moistened with egg white on the eye;
et li chiés dou malaide soit en ton sain et met ton doi mostrant sus la medicine, et presse I poc et lou muef toutes les fois que li malaide sent mordication de la medicine, car il sent mordication ausi com de feu.	And the patient's head should be on your right and place your left hand over the medicine, and press the cup and cloth every time the patient feels a tingling from the medicine, for they feel it as if from fire.
Quant tu as ceu fait longement, si oste la medicine a ton doit.	When you have done this for a long time, then remove the medicine at its proper time.
Et quant li mordication sera passee, si leve le leu d’awe, et rewarde se tu vois la papiere levee ausi com s’ele estoit levee par constraignement de feu ou par incision;	And when the tingling has passed, lift the area of the application, and observe if you see the paper lifted as if it were raised by the constraint of fire or by an incision;
et s’il est ensi, si est bien.	And if it is thus, then it is well.
Se ceu non, si remet encor de la medicine sus lou leu ou li medicine n’ait ovreit, tant que tes ovraiges soit igalz, et tes eulz mis a point;	If not, then reapply the medicine to the place where it was applied until your work is even, and your eyes are set properly;
puis met sus coton moilliet en burre tant que li keurs ars soit cheus, aprés cure le leu de l’oignement qui est apelez «dyafenis» et d’autre, tant qu’il soit sanez.	then apply moistened cotton with butter until the burned area is covered, and then treat the ointment site which is called "diaphysis" and others, until it is healed.
Et se t’est mestier que tu te warde bien a ton ovraige par grant warde qu’il ne chiece point de la medicine as eulz.	And if it is necessary for you to be very careful with your work so that none of the medicine gets into your eyes.
Et se li papiere devient mole aprés, et li poil poignent en l’oil, si recomence la medicine sus celui leu qui est mollifiez de la papiere proprement, ensi com tu as fait devant;	And if the paper becomes soft after that, and the hair irritates the eye, then reapply the medicine to the softened area properly, as you did before;
aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	then treat it until it is healed;
et c’est li forme de la fuelle dou mirte:	and this is the form of the leaf of myrtle:
Et saichés que li eul des homes sont divers en grandor et en petitece, et selonc ceu soit tes constraignemens;	And note that the eyes of people vary in size and smallness, and adjust accordingly your treatments;
et ne soit mie reponue li droite voie a celui cui est li estude de cest art.	and do not dismiss the proper way for those who study this art.
de la cure de fistule par cautere	for the treatment of fistula by cautery
Quant tu cures fistule si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladies, et tes cures ne profitent mie, adonques covient il que tu li fais cautere selonc ceste maniere.	When you treat a fistula as we have said in the division of diseases, and your treatments are ineffective, then it is necessary that you perform a cautery according to this method.
Comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain;	Instruct the patient to place his head on your lap;
et teigne li menistres son chief entre tes mains en teil maniere qu’il ne se mueve, ne ne demoinne son chief;	and hold the patient's head between your hands in such a way that it does not move, nor should he shift his head;
aprés met coton moilliet en abin d’uef ou en jus de persillion sus l’oil;	then place moistened cotton in vinegar or parsley juice on the eye;
aprés chaufe le cautere qui est teilz:	After heating the cautery which is similar:
et est chevez au chief si com li forme d’une penne de vouteul, ensamble la queil soit li cautere;	and place it on the head as the shape of a quill feather, so that the entire cautery is aligned;
se tu vues, si soit apointé des l’un chief dusc’a l’autre, et se tu vues, si soit ausi com une tente;	if you wish, it should extend from one side of the head to the other, and if you prefer, it should be like a tent;
mais toutevoie, cist qui est chevez vaut mues por ton ovraige.	but in any case, this position is better for your work.
Aprés presse la fistule s’ele est overte, et en trai la porriture, et la seche;	After pressing the open fistula and removing the pus, dry it;
et s’ele est close, si la oevre, et trai fuers la bowe;	and if it is closed, work on it and draw out the humor;
aprés met sus le cautere chaut forment, et tien ta main au cautere a la partie dou neif ensus de l’oil, que ta mains ne faice folie;	After place the hot cautery, and hold your hand on the cautery at the part of the nose above the eye, so that your hand does not act foolishly;
et met le cautere en la graisse de l’oil, et la corromp.	and place the cautery in the fat of the eye, and it corrupts.
Se tu viens au comencement dou cautere jusc’a l’os, si serait bien.	If you proceed to the beginning of the cautery up to the bone, it would be well.
Se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere encor une fois, et autre se tu en as mestier, et le laisse III jors;	If not, then begin the cautery again once more, and another if you need it, and leave it for three days;
aprés i met sus coton moilliet en burre, et lou cure de l’oignement desiccatif tant qu’il soit sanez, et se XL jors passent qu’il ne soit sanez, si met sus medicine ague corrosive tant que li os soit descovers;	after place cotton moistened in butter, and the treatment of a dry ointment until it is healed, and if forty days pass and it is not healed, then place a watery corrosive medicine until the bone is exposed;
et lou reis selonc ceu que il venrait en son chapistre.	and the king according to what he would come in his chapter.
Et i a une maniere de cautere de fistule que aucun des anciens dirent.	And there is a method of cautery for fistulas that some of the ancients described.
Entens a fistule, et fens le leu;	Attend to the fistula, and clean the area;
aprés met en la fendure I camahan subtil de coi ci est li forme:	after placing in the opening a fine piece of wax, here is the form it should take:
et i font a la quantiteit d’une .З. de plonc;	and make it in the quantity of one ounce;
et tien ta main ou camahan fermement, et ne se mueve li malaides nes point, que li plons fondus ne corre a son oil;	and hold your hand on the wax firmly, and do not let the patient move at all, so that the melted wax does not run into their eye;
et covient c’on mette sus l’oil a malaide coton moilliet en abin d’uefz ou en awe:	and it is necessary to place over the patient's eye cotton moistened in egg whites or honey:
li plonc si art lou leu de fistule, et lou saine per mervillouse saniteit.	the poultice should be applied to the area of the fistula, and it will heal wonderfully.
Et se li fistule est sanee per le cautere que nos avons dit, c’est boin.	And if the fistula is healed by the cautery that we have mentioned, it is good.
Se ce non, si covient aministrer pertus au neif, et ramener la fistule au cors dou neif selonc ceu qu’il covient en som propre leu.	If not, it is necessary to administer a puncture with a knife, and bring the fistula back into the body of the knife according to what is proper in its own place.
des crevaices en levres	of cracks in the lips
Mout de fois avienent crevaices en levres que sont apelees «poil», et meismement en levres des enfans.	Often there are cracks in the lips which are called "hairs," especially in the lips of children.
Quant tu cures ces crevaices de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et li cure ne profite, adonques eschaufe I petit cautere cultellaire selonc ceste forme:	When you treat these cracks as we have said in the divisions, and the treatment does not help, then heat a small knife-shaped cautery according to this form:
Et le met hastanment en celles crevaices tant qu’il viegne jusc’a font;	And place it quickly into those crevices until it comes to the top;
aprés cure le leu de cerote tant qu’il soit sanez.	after treating the area with plaster until it is healed.
de l’aposteme de la goule	of the abscess of the cheek/gullet
Quant apostume vient en la racine de la goule ou en l’uve, ou ou palais, ou as racines des dens, aprés fait porriture et ront et est enveillis et devient fistule;	When an abscess comes to the root of the gums or in the uvula, or at the palate, or at the roots of the teeth, it becomes putrid and swollen and grows old and becomes a fistula;
et tu le cures si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie:	and you treat it as we have said in the divisions, and it does not improve:
adonques covient il que tu aies I cautere selonc la quantiteit de la fistule;	then you must use the cautery according to the size of the fistula;
aprés le bote ou pertus de la fistule, et tien ta main tant que li fer chaus viegne au font de li, et ou derrien leu;	after the opening or passage of the fistula, and hold your hand until the hot iron reaches its depth, and at the far end;
et fai ensi une fois ou II, aprés le cure de ce que nos avons dit en cures, tant qu’il soit sanez;	and do thus once or twice after the treatment of what we have said in treatments, until it is healed;
et s’il est curez ensi, c’est boin;	and if it is treated thus, it is good;
et se ceu non, si covient descovrir le leu et oster l’os corrumput, selonc ceu que vos le troverez en son chapistre.	and if not, it is necessary to uncover the place and remove the corrupted bone, according to what you will find in its chapter.
dou movement des dens	of the movement of the teeth
Quant les gencives sont mollifies par moistor et les dens muevent, et tu le cures per medicines et ceu ne vaut, adonc met le chief dou malaide en ton sain;	When the gums soften due to moisture and the teeth become loose, and you treat it with medicine but that is ineffective, then place the patient's head on your lap;
aprés eschaufe le cautere dont li forme venra ci aprés en teil maniere que tu mettes une cainne sor le dent;	after heating the cautery in such a manner that you place a chain on the tooth;
et met dedens le cautere chaut hastanment, et tien tant ta main que li malaides sente la chalor venant a la racine dou dent;	and put quickly into the cautery hot heat, and hold so long that the patient feels the heat coming to the root of the tooth;
aprés lieve ta main et rencomence le cautere selonc ta volenteit;	after lift your hand and restart the cautery according to your will;
aprés emplisse li malaides sa bouche d’awe salee, et la teigne une houre et raiche fuers.	after fill the patient's mouth with salt water, and let it stay for one hour and rinse out afterwards.
Et en teil maniere li dens qui estoit movans si est confermez, et li gencive mollifie restrainte, et li moistors corrumpue sechie.	And in this manner, the tooth that was moving becomes fixed, and the softened gum is restrained, and the corrupted moisture dries up.
de la dolor des dens	of the pain of the teeth
Quant dolor de dens vient por froidor, ou il i a froidor ou veir, et les cures de medicine ne valent, adonc i ait mestier de cautere selonc II manieres:	When tooth pain comes from cold, where there is actual coldness, and medical treatments are ineffective, then there is need for cautery according to two methods:
et cautere de burre et cautere de feu.	and cautery with leather and cautery with fire.
Cautere de burre si est telz que tu preignes burre de vaiche, et le bout en une cuillier de fer ou d’arain;	Cautery with leather is such that you take leather from the hide, and cut it into a spoon-shaped piece of iron or brass;
aprés pren coton et envolope sus la pointe d’une tente, et la moille en burre bulit, et met sus le dent dolant hastanment et tien tant qu’il soit refroidiez;	After take cotton and wrap around the tip of a needle, and melt it in butter boiled, and apply to the aching tooth quickly and keep until it is cooled;
et ensi fai sovent tant que sa vertus viegne a la racine de la dent, et se tu vues si moille laine et coton en burre froit, et met sus le dent doillant, et met sus I fer chaut tant que li feus viegne au chevement dou dent.	and thus do often until its virtue reaches the root of the tooth, and if you wish to melt wool and cotton in cold butter, and apply it to the aching tooth, and place hot iron on it until the heat reaches the top of the tooth.
Li cauteres ensamble feu si est telz que tu preignes uns cainne de fer ou d’arain, et soit grosse si que li feus ne viegne a la bouche dou malaide;	The fire cautery is such that you take a piece of iron or copper, and let it be thick so the heat does not reach the patient's mouth;
aprés chaufe le cautere, de coi li forme venra ci aprés, et le met sus le dent et tien ta main tant que li cauteres soit refroidiez;	After heat the cautery, from which the form will come next, and apply it to the tooth and hold your hand until the cautery is cooled;
fai ceu sovent, car li dolor sera ostee celui jor meisme ou l’endemain.	Do this often, for the pain will be removed on that very day or the next.
Et covient que li malaides emplisse sa bouche de boin burre en l’empressement de cel cautere, et puis le raiche fuer;	And it is necessary that the patient fill their mouth with good butter at the time of this cautery, and then lie still;
et c’est li forme dou cautere:	and this is the form of the cautery:
Et fai cautere dou queil chief que tu voudras, et selonc ceu que tu as pooir;	And apply the cautery to whichever area you wish, according to your ability;
et c’est li forme de la caine:	and this is the form of the cane:
des scrophules	scrofulas
Quant les scrophules sont de fleume et de moistors froides, et ne sont obeissans a digestion par medicines, adonques eschaufe le cautere cheveit de coi ci aprés vient li forme, et ait II aovertures por les fumees a issir au cautere de l’autre partie;	When scrofulas are of phlegm and cold moisture, and do not respond to digestion through medicine, then heat the cautery as described below in its form, and have two openings for the smoke to escape from the opposite side of the cautery;
et met le cautere chaut sus l’apostume une fois, ou II se mestier est, tant qu’il viegne au font de l’apostume;	and place the hot cautery on the abscess once or twice as needed until it reaches the bottom of the abscess;
et se li apostume est petis si met cautere selonc la quantiteit de l’apostume, et le laisse ensi III jors;	and if the abscess is small, place the cautery according to its size, and leave it like this for three days;
et met sus coton moilliet em burre tant que li arsure soit ostee;	and apply moist wool wrapped in butter until the burn is gone;
aprés cure le leu d’oignemens et de tentes tant qu’il soit sanez.	after treating the area with ointments and bandages until it is healed.
Li forme de la cainne:	The form of the cautery:
Quant les moistors vainquent sus les chenals dou pormon, et meismement quant ce vient de froide complexion, adonc covient que li malaides soit voidiez premiers par medicines solutives;	When the moistures overpower in the channels of the body, especially when it comes from cold temperament, then the patient must first be treated with solvent medications.
aprés li fai cautere a la racine de la gorge, et te garde que tu ne venir mie jusc’a la gorge, et n’ardre dou keur mais c’un poc.	After you make a cautery at the root of the throat, be careful not to go up to the throat, and do not burn near the heart but just a little.
Aprés li fai I autre cautere a la jointure dou col au chief de l’espinee, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» de coi nos avons la forme devant;	After you make another cautery at the joint of the neck to the top of the spine, and let the cauterizations which are called "clavile" be as we have described their form before;
et cure le leu si com nos avons devant dit tant qu’il soit sanez.	and treat the area as we said before until it is healed.
de la toust	of coughing
Quant tous et maladie de pormon sont de moistors froides, et li malaides nen ait fievre ne sechor, et est li maladie anciaine, se li fai .II cauteres sus la forcele en leus vuis;	When all the diseases of paralysis are caused by cold moisture, and the patient has no fever or dryness, and the disease is old, then make two cauterizations on the forearm in their places;
et I autre cautere emmi le pis entre II mameles;	And the other cautery between two mammary glands;
et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» selonc la forme qui est devant dite.	And let the cautery called "clavile" be according to the form previously described.
Et se tu vues, fai cautere en poignant a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins» de coi li forme est ci devant en la maladie des oreilles;	And if you wish, make a cautery by pricking the entire cautery called "poins" for which the form is described above in the disease of the ears;
et soient li poins jusc’a XXX, ou enqui entor.	And let the points be up to thirty, or inquire around for this practice.
Aprés cure le leu selonc ceu qui est devant dit, et soit li cauteres a III rains selonc ceste forme:	After treating the area as described previously, let the cauterizations be three times according to this form:
Et por ceu sont li cautere plus legier, por ceu que tu en fais III a cop.	And because the cauterizations are lighter, do three of them at once.
de la dislocation de l’ajutoire	of the dislocation of the shoulder
Quant li chiés de l’ajutoire est desaloiez par cause de moistor, et on le remet a leu, et il n’i puet demorer ains revient adés et desalue par petit movement qui avient, si com nos avons esproveit, adonques covient il que tu ramoinnes la dislocation premierement.	When the head of the shoulder is dislocated due to moisture, and it is reset but cannot stay in place, repeatedly dislocating with slight movements as we have experienced, then you must first reset the dislocation.
Aprés soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos et sus son costeit;	After have the patient lie on their back and side;
aprés lieve le keur qui est dedens le titillite as dois de ta main senestre;	then lift the knee that is inside the thigh with both of your left hand;
et se li jointure est desaluee dedens, si eschaufe le cautere qui a II ners douqueil ci est li forme:	And if the joint is dislocated inside, heat the cautery which has two edges of copper; this is its form:
et cauterize lou keur tant qu’il le perce jusc’a costeit, et venrait li fugure dou cautere ensamble IIII cauteres;	And cauterize the skin until it pierces to the bone, and the shape of the cautery will result in four cauterizations;
et por ceu est faite cautere avec le cautere qui a III ners, por coi li figure de cauterization sunt sis cauteres;	And for that reason, the cautery is made with a cautery that has three edges, which results in six shapes of cauterizations;
et sont li nerf selonc la subtiliteit d’une tente et c’est li forme dou cautere qui a III ners:	And the nerve is as fine as a thread, and this is the form of the cautery that has three edges:
Et aucune fois est ajostez sus ce I nerf por coi il i a VIII cauteres.	And sometimes it is adjusted on this one handle, so there are eight cauteries.
Aprés met sus le cautere porrelz broiez avec seil;	After placing the cautery, put on crushed herbs with salt;
aprés fai reposer le malaide, et ne soit meus li membres par lonc tens tant qu’il soit bien confortez.	After having the patient rest, do not move the limb for a long time until it is well settled.
Et s’il est desaloiez desus, liquelz chose avient poc, adonques fait cautere sus l’epaisse dou cautere clavile, ou mout de cauteres en poignant.	And if it is dislocated above, which thing happens rarely, then make a cautery on the thick part of the cautery nodule, or many cauteries in pricking.
Car li jointure est refermee, et est ostee li moistor et est sanez li malaides.	For the joint is closed, and the moisture is removed and the patient is healed.
Quant en l’estomac vienent froidures et mout de moistors tant qu’il l’estraient a sa complexion, et sont multipliet li catharre a lui, et es manieres de cures acostumees et il ne profite mie, adonc covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus son dos, et estende ses jambes et ses mains.	When coldness and much moisture come to the stomach such that it strains its constitution, and the catarrh is multiplied within him, and in the usual methods of cure he finds no benefit, then it must be that the patient be laid on his back, and stretch out his legs and hands.
De ceu en aprés li fai III cauteres I desoz la cuillier dou pis per la quantiteit d’un doi, a tout le cautere clavile, et II cauteres defuers les II costez tant que li figure des cauteres soit a III angles, et ait teil espaice entre l’une et l’autre qu’elles ne soient jointes ensamble quant elles giteront porriture;	From then on, perform three cauterizations. Open the pus container with the spoon of pitch in the quantity of two doses, for the entire cautere clavile, and two cauterizations outside the two sides until the figure of the cauterizations forms at three angles, and keep such a space between one and the other that they do not join together when they discharge pus.
et soient li cautere si parfont qu’il porpreignent les II pars dou keur, et soit li figure des cauteres selonc ceste forme sens ajostement:	and let the cauterizations be deep enough to reach both sides of the chest, and let the shape of the cauterizations follow this form without adjustment:
Et se tu vues cauterize d’un grant cautere enmi l’estomac selonc ceste forme;	And if you wish to cauterize with a large cauterization in the middle of the stomach according to this form;
et celui qui avra paour de cest cautere, cauterize en poignant et seigne sus l’estomac i. point selonc la quantiteit que tu vues d’enche;	And he who fears this cautery, cauterize by pricking and cutting one point on the stomach according to the quantity you wish of it;
puis le cauterize a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins».	then cauterize with the entire cautery which is called "points".
Aprés le cure de la cure que nos avons eut devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	After the treatment of the condition we had before, as long as it is healed.
Quant au foie vient dolor de froit et de moistor et de grosse ventositeit, tant qu’il est fuer mis de sa complexion natureil per les superfluitez;	When the liver suffers pain from cold and moisture and from excessive gas, to such an extent that it is weakened from its natural temperament by excesses;
et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne li profite mie, si covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus son haitereil;	and the patient is treated with what we have said in the divisions, and it does not help him, then it is necessary that the patient be bled from his head;
et signe d’enche III cauteres selonc ceste forme et ceste figure et ceste quantiteit sus lou foie, defuer les ypocondres, lai ou li coutes de l’ome vient;	and mark three cauterizations according to this form and this figure and this quantity on the liver, away from the hypochondriac regions, where the ribs of a person are;
et ait d’espaice entre chaicun cautere la groissece d’un doi;	and there should be a space between each cauterization equal to the thickness of a finger;
et soient li cautere dou lonc dou cors, et ne presser mie mout ta main a tot le cautere;	and let the cauterization be along the length of the body, and do not press too hard with your hand along the entire cauterization;
et soit arse tant soulement li moitiez dou keur, et soit li malaides drois sus ses piez;	and let it be burned only halfway up the heart, and let the patient stand straight on his feet;
et s’il ne peut, si soit gisans, et estende ses jambes, et lieve ses brais;	and if he cannot stand, let him lie down, and extend his legs, and raise his arms;
et c’est li forme:	and this is the form:
Et se ta volentez est, si cauterize ces cauteres dou cutellaire, se tu es subtilz et saiges en l’art, et te warde que tu n’ardes mie tout le keur, car tu feroies sechier tout le cors;	And if your intention is to cauterize these cauterizations on the scapula, do so if you are skilled and wise in the art, but beware that you do not burn the entire heart, for you would dry out the whole body;
et qu’il ne viegne jusc’a boueil, car li keurs est mout subtilz lai endroit, et lou saiches por voir.	and let it not reach the eye, for the vein is very delicate there, and you should know this well.
Quant il a apostume au foie, et tu vues savoir s’il est en la char dou foie ou en la toile:	When there is an abscess in the liver, and you wish to know if it is in the flesh of the liver or in the membrane:
s’il est en la char, se sent li malaides dolor ne mie trop fort;	if it is in the flesh, the patient feels pain, but not too strong;
et s’il est en la toile, si sent dolor forsenee.	and if it is in the membrane, the patient feels intense pain.
Et lors quant ceste cure desoit les mires, si covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus sa teste;	And when this treatment requires the use of leeches, it is necessary that the patient lie on their head;
et puis seigne d’enche le leu ou li apostumes est, et puis chaufe le cautere qui est semblans au rais, de coi ci est li forme:	and then mark the spot where the abscess is, and then heat the cautery which resembles a reed, as described in this form:
Et cauterize I cautere tant que li keurs soit ars, et viegne jusc’a syphac, tant que li porreture soit toute fuers;	And cauterize the cautery until the flesh is burned, and it reaches to sepsis, until all the corruption is burnt away;
aprés la cure selonc la cure des essues tant qu’il soit sanez;	after the treatment according to the treatment of blisters until it is healed;
et ne covient mie que de cest cautere use nuls fuers que cil qui ait estudieit longement en l’art de medicine, et par cui mains cestes maladies ont corrut aucune fois.	and it is not appropriate for anyone other than those who have studied medicine extensively to use this cautery, and by whose hands these diseases have been cured at times.
Adonques puet il hardiement ovrer, et toutevoies il me semble que mues vaut li laissier.	Then he may boldly proceed with the operation, yet it seems to me that waiting would be better.
dou cautere de pleuresin	for the cautery of pleurisy
Li ancien dirent que on doit faire a pleuresin cauteres de racines d’aristologe, et en teil maniere:	The ancients said that one should make cauteries for ulcers using the roots of aristolochia, and in such a manner:
pren une racine d’aristologe longe, la plus grant que tu poras troveir, et soit seche, et soit ausi grosse et ausi longe comme tes dois;	take a root of aristolochia as long as you can find, and let it be dry, and as thick and as long as your thumb;
et la moille en oile, et l’emprens au feu, et cauterize I cautere entre la forcele et lou col, et II petis cauteres un poc en dessendant en la partie qui est desoz la barbe;	And the grease in oil, and press it to the fire, and I cauterize between the neck and jaw, and II small cauters a little descending in the part which is below the beard;
et II cauteres entre la quinte coste et la sisime, en declinant derrier un poc;	And II cauters between the fifth and sixth rib, inclining backward a little;
et I cautere emmi le pis, et I autre sus l’estomac, et I entre II espaules, et II as II costez dou pis defuers le cautere qui est entre II espaules;	And I cauter between the heels, and one above the stomach, and one between the two shoulders, and two at the sides of the buttocks outside the cauter which is between the two shoulders;
et ne presser mie ta main, ains fai apertement ausi com en odorant.	And do not press your hand, but rather do it openly as when smelling.
Et dirent aucun ancien que aucun home usent de cautere de feir semblant a I raseur, et l’eschaufent et le mettent entre les costes, tant qu’il vient a cel aposteme;	And some ancient ones say that some people use a fire cautery resembling a razor, and heat it up and place it between the ribs until it reaches the abscess;
et saut fuers li dolor, si com nos avons dit en l’aposteme dou foie.	And the pain jumps out, as we have said regarding the abscess of the liver.
