Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans, et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut:	I say that when a simple wound comes to the head, and the bone is not broken, be careful if it is from falling stones or similar things, and the skin is completely torn and the wound is large, and you fear the rise of a hot abscess:
si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree;	If you treat it immediately to staunch the bleeding from the head itself if little blood comes from the wound, and let the bandage be on the opposite side of the injured part;
et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	and prevent the patient from overindulging in wine and heavy meats.
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char;	And if he does not want to be bled, then let his meat intake be reduced, and do not drink wine, nor eat meat.
et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice;	and place on the wound, if small abscesses occur, cotton soaked in rose oil only, or in styptic wine;
et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés;	and if there is no hot abscess, then apply to the wound, if it is fresh with all its blood and has not been exposed to air, a powder which I will describe shortly;
et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound has been moved, apply some ointments until it is healed.
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	And if the wound is large like a sword cut and similar ones, and the lips cannot be brought together by tents, then sew them together, as I will describe for belly wounds and sutures.
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope;	If the wound is exposed bone and pus, and barely holds together in one spot, cut it;
puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir, et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	then treat the wound with medication, and replace hard tissue in place of skin, and instruct the patient to eat coarse foods, such as brains and boiled wheat, as well as pulses, and similar things.
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure;	And if you find on the skin putrefaction that does not adhere to the bone, cut away all the putrid flesh, and apply forceful treatment, then treat it;
et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil;	and if there is an artery in the wound or vein that cannot be cauterized, and it cannot be staunched with medicine, then tie off the artery, and if you find it dislocated, secure it with a thread;
et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	And if this does no good, then cauterize it.
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere:	And if these wounds are small and simple, the treatment is easy:
et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	and it is that you put in this powder which the patient should sprinkle as the fire has moved.
Et li maniere de la poudre si est:	And the manner of the powder is as follows:
pren encens une partie;	take one part of incense;
sanc de dragon II parties;	dragon's blood two parts;
chalz vive III parties, et le poudre subtilment, et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc;	living charcoal three parts, and powder it finely, then apply to the wound and press firmly until it sticks well and adheres to all its blood;
et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle;	and then stir the poultice well, and leave it on without removing it, unless it swells;
car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	for one should not remove the medicine until she is healed.
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	And sometimes one uses charcoal alone when one does not have incense or dragon's blood, but the burn has moved the wound.
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre;	And if the burn has moved the wound, especially in winter, one must not use this powder on it;
mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe;	but apply some digestible ointments, or a poultice made of oat flour with water and honey, until it discharges pus;
puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	then treat it further until he is healed.
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz;	And if the fracture of a bone comes with the wound, and it is small, then extract it with fine forceps;
et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	And I will tell you hereafter about fractures of the head.
de la plaie dou col	of the wound of the neck
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	If the wound is on the neck and it is simple, there is no difference between it and that of the head, but if the nerve of the neck or the artery is cut.
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire;	If it is the nerve, then there is no other treatment but to leave it untreated, and not apply anything constricting, for it harms the nerve and causes it to retract;
et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres;	and do not apply anything cold to the wound, for the substance of the nerves is cold, and their continuation is with the brain, which is the highest part of the body;
mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce, et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	but let the medicine be warm, such as chalts washed in sweet water and mixed with rose oil, and copper leaves also washed in sweet water, and other mineral stones in this manner, and moist ointments.
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound is large, then sew and ligature with bandages, then treat it until he is healed.
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu;	And if the wounds are deep and she is swollen and full of pus, then pierce it at a lower place;
et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est;	and if the artery is cut and blood begins to flow out, then stop it, tie it off, and cauterize it if necessary;
et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va, si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel;	and if the spine of the neck is cut by the sword, and the conduit through which flesh passes is guarded, then sew up the wound on top of the windpipe, and do not touch the throat but reset it according to its natural position;
et puis l’estraint avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez;	and then bind it carefully, and leave it for several days, then treat it with drying ointments until it is healed;
et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier;	and if the wound has made an impression on the bone, then probe it;
et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse, et soit desevree et aligie li issue;	and if there are fragments of bone, remove them all as far as you can; and those that you cannot reach, leave until the wound heals and then separate and align the opening.
et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	and if the wound is fresh, then sprinkle on the powder that I have mentioned.
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	And if there is bone in the wound and there is an abscess, then treat it as I have said in its chapter.
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	of the wound from a spear or knife
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne:	If it is a wound from a spear or knife, and the wound is deep, then look to see if air bubbles come out of the wound when the patient inhales:
saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz;	you then know that the wound is fatal;
et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont, et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide;	and if it is not deep, and it is fresh with all its blood, do not put the powder at the first hour, nor bind it for the blood that does not stop flowing, and return to the heart, and kill the patient;
mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie II fois le jor;	but apply an attracting ointment and bind it twice a day;
et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor, et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie III jors, ou IIII, ou plusors;	and if you do not have an ointment, place old cotton in the wound to absorb the moisture, and make the patient sleep on the wound for three days, or four, or more;
si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’estraingnemens d’alainne;	then no spasm will come, nor will there be any harmful trembling or alienation of the heart;
et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	And when you see good signs, then know that the wound is safe.
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then cure her with poultices and other treatments until she is well;
et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule;	and if she cannot recover, and you treat her, then know that there is an abscess;
si la cure si com on doit.	treat her as one should.
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant;	And if the wound is from a sword or knife cut, and it is simple, or worse on the back, then treat it as one would in front;
s’elle est grans, de cousture;	if it is large, with sutures;
et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez;	and if it is small, with powder; and if it is pressed against the bone, and in pieces, then seek the wound, and treat the torn tendons if they are separated;
et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions;	and if they are not separated, let the wound heal, which will ease the extraction;
et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	and for other wounds on other limbs, the judgment is as we have said.
dou derrompement dou ventre	of the rupture of the abdomen
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis;	The rupture of the abdomen is great, medium, and small;
de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus;	in the large wound, sometimes the intestines protrude, or the nerves of the intestines, which requires their replacement;
et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans, por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut;	and the suturing is more difficult, and sometimes a small wound is worse than a large one because if the intestines are not replaced gradually, they can be pushed back in too quickly;
por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes, et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres II.	because the intestines swell immediately when they feel the cold, so they are pushed back in more forcefully, and because of this, a smaller wound is worse, since replacing the intestine to its place happens differently than with others.
Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc IIII manieres:	And know that a rupture of the abdomen occurs according to four manners:
les II costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre, et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et II autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies;	the two common sutures occur in the seam of the abdomen, and the suture of other wounds of the body and two other specific sutures are common to other wounds;
et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	and they are still more specific to the seam of the abdomen, and I will describe each one and clarify.
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer, et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des II manieres:	I say that when the wound is small, and some part of the intestine protrudes, and it is a difficult thing to replace, this is done by one of the two methods:
ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit, ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	either because of the smallness of the wound, as we have said, or because the intestines are swollen due to cold.
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere:	And when it is cold, warm it in such a manner:
moillie une esponge ou I mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement, ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique, et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee;	moisten a sponge or a piece of cloth in warm water only, or boil it in hot water with thuja, cypress, and spikenard, and rinse the intestine until the swelling subsides;
et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	and sometimes use restraining wine, which is muddy and has sediment to reduce swelling.
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites, car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose;	And when you see the swelling begin to subside, moisten the intestine with water or broth made from hellebore and mallows that have been cooked, for this gradually opens the passage.
et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes;	and if it cannot enter, make a small incision in the wound with the instrument used for cutting hemorrhoids;
et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille, que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait;	and the first treatment is to avoid cutting, as one should not cut there unless there is great necessity.
et c’est li estrumens por le fendre:	and this is the instrument for cutting:
si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	cut inside along the curve and not away from it, and see here the form:
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer, si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre, se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	And when the wound is enlarged, and the intestines jump out, put them back in their natural place if you have the power, for this is better.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre, si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief;	When the wound is wide and it is in the part below the belly, you should have the patient lie on his back, and raise his legs higher than his head;
et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre, si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz, et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des II parties si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre;	and if it is in the part below the belly, raise the head and feet higher than the affected parts, and similarly, if the rupture of the abdomen is on one of the two sides, place the injured side higher than the other;
et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	And thus you must administer what I say regarding large and medium wounds.
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet, puis aies entre tes mains I ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main, et assemble les levres;	In small wounds, apply what is appropriate for them, then hold the dressing in your hands which covers the entire wound opening, and bring together the edges.
et c’est la maniere commune de costures, et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie, puis laisse des le chief de la plaie I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait I boin fil fort;	and this is the common method of suturing, which involves taking one or more needles according to the width of the wound, then leaving some space at the top of the wound and inserting a needle where there is strong thread.
et perce les II chiés dou cuir avec les II chiés dou siphac, qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie, et assemble les II chief dou siphac les IIII ensamble;	and pierce both sides of the skin with two needles, which are inside the skin from below, until you puncture it on that part, and bring together the two ends of the thread all together;
puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de II pars, puis assemble les II chiés de la plaie avenanment, et puis laisse I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille;	Then take a thread doubled around the needle on both sides, then bring together the two edges of the wound, and leave one space, and insert another needle;
puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille, et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles, tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte;	Then tie the thread around the needle as you did with the first needle, and continue doing so as needed for the number of needles required until the entire wound is closed.
et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses, car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer:	and the needles should be medium-sized, between fine and coarse, because fine needles cut through the flesh entirely, and overly thick ones cannot enter properly:
por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes;	that is why they should be medium-sized;
et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir, k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure;	and it is not appropriate to insert the needles too far from the flesh and skin, as they may cut and damage the wound before it heals;
et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir, et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir, et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee;	and then cut the tips of the needles so they do not prick the patient while sleeping, and put tents or cloths over the needle tips to keep them from moving, and leave them until the wound is sealed;
et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies, car il i soffist une aguille ou II.	and this method of suturing with needles is more suitable for small wounds, because it only requires one or two needles.
Li seconde costure si est commune, et est que tu assemble les II chiés dou cuir et les II chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait I fort fil moien;	The second method of suturing is common, and it involves bringing together the two edges of the skin and the two edges of the underlying tissue with one needle or thread that is strong.
et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz IIII ensamble, si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras;	and when you have pierced all four edges together, pull the needle back to the part where you started, in the manner of sewing cloth;
et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi;	and place a space between each seam the thickness of a small bean;
ceste costure sevent li home, et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre, qui estoit navrez d’un coutel, et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant, et issoit des intestines bien II palmes de grant, et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	This seam is known to the surgeon, and I sewed a wound that a man had in his abdomen, which was pierced by a knife, and the wound was more than one palm wide, and intestines came out about two palms long, and the wound was within the abdomen.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit XXIIII houres fuer, et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a XV jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	I returned the intestine to him after it had been outside for twenty-four hours, and the wound was sealed up until fifteen days, and I treated him, and he was well.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle;	And the physicians had judged that he would die, and this was a miracle;
et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en I leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines;	and I did not treat it with ointment, for I was in a place where none could be found, nor any medicine;
et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel II fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	and I would place old cotton on the wound twice a day, and wash it with honey water until it was healed.
Or vos dirai les II propres manieres de cousture:	Now I will tell you the two proper methods of suturing:
pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens;	take the needle, and bring it from the outer part to the inner part;
quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille, et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer;	when it has pierced the skin straight through, lay the tip of the thread or suture where you inserted the needle, and have it pierce from the inner part to the outer part;
et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz, et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	and the understanding of this suture is that you sew as tailors do with skins, and leave one end on one side, and take it up on the other, until the entire suture is complete.
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement, si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les II parties ensamble naturelment, et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere:	The second method of suturing, which Galenus described properly, is like this: some people bring together the two parts naturally, and join one end of the suture to the other in such a manner:
fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement, et laisse les II chiés dou syfac;	Insert a needle into the head of the thumb nearby, and pierce only that place, and leave the two heads of the shoulder alone;
puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, as II chiés dou syfac;	then turn the needle and pierce from the outer part to the inner part, through the two heads of the shoulder;
puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en II autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit;	then pierce one and the other from the outer part to the inner part, in two other heads of the thumb that are on the opposite side;
et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	and this is the most proper method of suturing and the most common.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent, c’on doit coudre le ventre a II aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune;	Galien says this and some testify that one should suture the abdomen with two needles, each having its own thread;
et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies;	And one must insert one needle from one side, and the other from the opposite side, in the manner of those who sew belts;
et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre, si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	And know that when the rupture is in the middle of the belly, the suturing is more difficult than for other places on the abdomen.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies:	The judgment of the wound is such as the judgment of other wounds:
et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee, si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout;	And it is when you find the wound fresh with all its blood, as if the arrow had drawn it, then reset the intestines and sew it up;
puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char, et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe;	Then apply powder that heals flesh, and if the arrow has drawn it, then apply any salve that is present until the wound absorbs it;
et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach;	And cut the thread, and let the stitches be sealed, and the wound;
puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez;	then treat the wound as with others, until it is healed;
et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel, et le remue II fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	and if you do not have medicine, place on it as soon as it begins to discharge, old cotton, and change it twice a day until it is healed.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples;	For you do not need other medicine in many cases where the wounds are simple;
et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz, si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset, et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles;	and if you fear that the wound may spread to the principal limbs, then it is necessary to moisten fine wool in warm infused oil or rose oil, and place it around the edges, and between the shoulders;
et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient, si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine;	And if he feels pain or putrefaction in the bowels, and this often happens, then administer an enema of boiled black wine to him, and especially if the putrefaction reaches the intestine;
et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	And pierce inside, and know that when it is the large intestine, it is easier to heal than the small one.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez, et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	The intestine called "jejunum" cannot heal when it is pierced, and this is due to the smallness of its veins that are there, and because of the subtlety of the entire body, and the proximity of its nature to the nerves.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres;	And if the spleen jumps out of the wound, put it back in as with the intestine, while it is fresh.
et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, car il i a voinnes et arteres;	And if it is old and has turned green or black, then you must tie off the area that is black so no more blood comes out, as there are veins and arteries there;
puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien, et met les II chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	Then cut away what is between the ligament, and hang the two heads from below the wound up to where the fibres fall off to ease the extraction when the splinters drop out, and the wound will heal.
de la routure dou boueil	of the fracture of the eye socket
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite, si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes, por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance;	When the intestines are pierced and the wound is small, it can sometimes be repaired in certain individuals, as I witnessed a man who was pierced in the abdomen with a lance;
et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac, et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez;	and the wound was on the right side of the stomach, and it became inflamed and developed into a fistula, from which feces and gas would escape;
je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	I treated it as best I could and did not stop suturing until he was healed, and the flesh grew together.
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre;	And when I saw him soldering it, I feared the patient would have pain in his abdomen;
et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans;	and he did not suffer any pain, but remained in better disposition, eating and drinking;
et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere:	and some experienced practitioners say that when there is a small wound in the intestine, it should be treated in such a manner:
pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie, et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les II levres, si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus;	take large pads and then bring the edges of the wound together, and when the pad has opened the mouth, place it on the two edges so that it holds them closed;
et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier, puis met I autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise;	and then cut the head of the pad, and it should be held in place so that it cannot come loose, then place another pad after in the same manner as before, until the entire wound is covered;
et cout la plaie.	And sew the wound.
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide, et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste, en teil maniere:	If the head enters the intestine and causes no harm to the patient, one can tie the intestine with a fine thread that is cut from an animal's intestine, in such a manner:
pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez, et puis lie au chief de cest fil I fil de lin subtil tort, puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure;	take the end of this intestinal thread that is very clean, and then tie a fine linen thread around it in a spiral, then insert the thread into the needle, and sew the intestine together, and knot it at the opening.
et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance;	and this method of stitching intestines is not stronger than according to the way of trust and hope;
et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	and if the wound is large and wide, especially when it is in one of the large intestines, there is no remedy or health, except for subtlety.
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	of a fistula wherever it may be
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule», et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	Know that any wound or abscess, when it begins to discharge, is generally called a "fistula," and especially when it is deep and goes inward.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor, et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil;	And a fistula is according to truth an irregular hard and white swelling where one does not feel pain, and it is also hairy like the feather of a bird;
et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse;	and sometimes it appears clear and hollow, and at other times thick;
aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez;	sometimes small, and at other times fairly large;
et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char, ce n’est fuers que par une des VIIII causes:	and I have spoken about this in the division of wounds, that every wound which is not healed and has no flesh, it is none other than due to one of the IX causes:
c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors;	that is to say, because of the smallness of the blood in the body;
ou por sa malice;	or due to its malice;
ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char;	For because there is hard flesh within, and on the lips, do not allow new flesh to grow;
ou il i a trop de bowe;	where there is too much swelling;
ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit;	when the pus is foul, and the matter is of poor quality;
ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure;	where the treatment with medicine is not good;
ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence;	for because the corruption is like that of pestilence;
ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature;	for because the property in the region has slow digestion, and delays health, and is swollen by nature;
ou il i a voinnes ou os:	where there are veins in the bone:
et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	and I have already shown all these causes, and the signs, and the remedies of medicine in the division.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	Now it is necessary for me to tell you about the treatment of a fistula which is done by handwork.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors;	Know that a fistula can occur in all parts of the body;
car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners, ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes, ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez;	for there are fistulas that occur in the large veins, and arteries, and nerves, in the face, or in the intestines, or in the bladder, or in some of the ribs, or in the spine, or in any joint of the hands or feet;
et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	and some affect the principal part of the limb and similar areas.
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance;	And all fistulas of this kind are difficult to heal, and there is no remedy except surgery, and ignorance;
et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure, et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier;	and if there is any fistula that does not reach the place I have mentioned, and you are confident in the treatment, and you wish to know it, then take a probe of brass or iron, if the fistula is straight, and insert it;
et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc, car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit;	and if the fistula is curved, then search with a fine probe of lead, for lead can bend around the curvature;
et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes, si la clisterize par l’un des pertus, car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie;	and if the fistula has multiple openings and you cannot properly probe it with probes, then irrigate through one of the openings, for the moisture passes quickly from one opening to another, and clean it;
puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont, et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent;	then probe carefully as best you can to determine if there are any bones or nerves involved, and feel thoroughly, and ask the patient well about the pain they feel when you press with your hand, and where they feel it;
et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine, ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit, et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens;	And when you truly know the place where it is, and if it is far from a joint, or a nerve, or an artery or a vein, or in any of the places that I have told you, then cut according to what I have said, and remove the pus and the corrupted flesh that are inside;
et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee, et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues, puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule, tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons;	And then treat it until it is healed, and if the fistula is deep in a straight line, you must cut deeply as much as possible, then place moistened tents in medicinal water, and put them up to the top of the fistula, until the medicine corrodes the excess that remains at the bottom;
et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez;	And then apply healing ointments to heal the flesh until it is healed;
et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit, et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	And if it is not healthy because of this, cauterize it as we have said, and if the bone is corrupted by the fistula, cut it away.
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit;	If a vein or nerve does not trouble the principal limbs as we have said;
et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee, puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez;	and if the bone is exposed, and there is corruption and blackening, then remove it until all corruption is gone, then treat with things that generate flesh until it is healthy;
et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant, saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font:	and if it is not healthy, and continues to swell as before, know that you have not gone far enough:
si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons, et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu;	then expose and search until you reach the bottom, and remove all the corruption, then restore the area;
et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	And if he is thus healthy, it is well.
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir;	If not, you should know that the corruption is too deep for you to reach.
si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature;	there is no other remedy but to leave it to nature;
et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles, si l’estrai a I estrument covenauble a ceu, et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un;	and if there is a small corrupt bone and you can pull it out with forceps, then extract it with the appropriate instrument, and if there are many bones, remove them all, do not leave even one.
et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour, si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	and if the moisture opposes you and there is no mistake or fear, then cut through the moisture and flesh, and free the bones.
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture, et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os, et adonc si avront plus legierement les os;	And if you cannot remove them at once, apply something to the wound that will promote putrefaction, and leave it until the flesh around the bones is rotten; then they will more easily have the bones removed.
et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse, si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee, puis restoure la plaie;	And if it is a large bone, such as from the leg or thigh, remove only the corruption until all the black matter is gone, then restore the wound;
et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os;	and if there is a large part of the corrupted tissue, and it reaches to the substance of the bone;
si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez;	it is necessary to wait and cover it up to the corruption, and then treat it until it is healed;
et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint I home en sa jambe, si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	and I will tell you about a fistula that occurred in a man's leg, so that you can take it as an example and aid in your work.
Il fut I jovencelz entor XXX ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors, tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir;	He was about thirty years old, who had pain in his leg from something that came inside the body, so much so that the matter reached the leg, and it swelled with a large abscess, and there was no reason to let out for opening.
mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri, et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors;	but the doctors, in their folly, operated so much on the abscess that they let out a great deal of matter, and it became a fistula, and many passages developed through which all flowed with pus and body moisture;
et maint mire i mirent cure entor II ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains, tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit, et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors;	and many doctors treated him for two years, and there was no skilled hand in the art until I was called to it, and I saw his leg and the medicines with which he was being treated, as well as what flowed out through the passages in large quantities.
et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	And the body of the young man became red, and he had a yellowish complexion.
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus, et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	I pitched a tent in one of these holes, and then searched all the holes, and found that they came together from all parts of the leg.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os, et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens;	I hurried then, and probed into one of the holes until I discovered part of the bone, which was corrupted and perforated, and the corruption extended to the bone inside;
je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai;	I treated what appeared to be the corrupted bone, and I believed there was no other corruption besides that which I removed;
et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder;	and began to heal the wound with internal medicines over a long period of time, and it could not close;
et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant, et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu;	and then I started again, and examined the bone as before, and found that the corruption continued in the bone, which I treated, and then removed it, and tried to close the place;
mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole, puis le restourai de medicines;	but I did not do so much as copy around a palm's breadth of the bone, and I treated it with force to its full extent, then restored it with medicines;
et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment, et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir, et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	and he was quickly healed and recovered, and there was no need to repeat the work except for the weakness of the patient, who could not endure it, and because of the fear of death that I had for him.
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement, et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	For often there was blood evacuation, but he remained entirely healthy, and in the place of the bone grew hard flesh, and he had good disposition without any harm or contrary effect whether going or coming.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere:	And if the bone is broken in any part of the body, it should be treated in this manner:
pren I liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert, et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut;	take some linen, and stretch it at the top of the bone that is exposed, and instruct someone to hold it up;
et met I autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os, et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz, et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char;	and place another bandage of woolen cloth thicker than the first linen, and bind it over the flesh that is around the bone, and stretch the top, so that you pull the corrupted flesh inward, and expose the flesh where you wish to treat, so that the bandage does not irritate the flesh;
et met I tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue;	and place a burning coal on a board beneath the bone to move aside the corrupted flesh;
et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	and continue scraping as long as possible until the corruption can be seen and felt, and scrape again several more times.
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie, si descuevre la char toute;	And if the bone is corrupted and it is not apparent, and the corruption is in the middle or a part of it, then uncover all the flesh.
puis met I tison desoz, et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption I poc, si com nos avons dit;	then place the coal beneath it, and then scrape from one part to the other the corrupted area, and let the scraper follow along with the extent of the corruption as we have said;
et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part;	and if the corruption is in the joint, then cut out the corrupted joint, and scrape the bone on the other side where it contains;
et se li corruptions est en la continuation des II jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper;	and if the corruption is in the continuation of the two joints, there is no other remedy but to cut;
et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose, mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert;	and if the corruption is in the joint of the hand or foot, it is very serious, but still you must inquire about that corruption, how it appears to you;
et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire;	and purify it in all ways that you can, but do not let the vein or nerve oppose you;
et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous, et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce;	and know that the incisions and saws for cutting these bones are many, according to the structure of the bone and its appearance, and their thickness and fineness, and their size and smallness, and their hardness;
et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument;	And for this reason, it is necessary to prepare for each kind of work its instrument;
et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art, et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies;	and know that the work will show you the instrument of which you will need, according to the knowledge of this art, and by the testimony of the manners of diseases;
si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	so consider the instrument of which you have need according to what is required.
dou feu	of fire
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer;	The head may become diseased either from within or from without;
et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie, si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient, si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre;	and when you have treated that corruption with the cure of medicines, and they do no good, then it is necessary to amputate that limb up to where the corruption comes, so that the patient escapes by this from death, or by the greater malice of losing the limb;
et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu, et porrist aprés la noiror, pues va celle corrosions de membre em membre, et prent par tout le cors;	And the signs are that the limb turns black, as if it were burned by fire, and then the blackness spreads, and this corruption of the limb spreads throughout the body.
si te haste dou coper, et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans, se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	Hasten to cut it, and if this is due to the bite of venomous beasts such as a sea scorpion and viper and similar ones, if the corruption is at the top of the head, then cut it, and do not give it space to reach the hand.
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras;	And if it reaches the hand, then cut at the joint so that the corruption does not reach the arm;
et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute;	and if it reaches the arm, then cut it with a knife;
et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors, et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut;	and if it exceeds the cut, it is fatal, and no remedy outside of its quantity of virtue helps;
et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet:	and do this entirely when corrosion comes to the foot:
s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe;	if it affects the first joint, then treat the next joint after it;
et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet;	and if it affects the foot, then treat the entire foot;
et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil;	and if it ascends to the leg, then treat at the knee joint;
et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort;	and if it comes above the knee, there is no other remedy but to let the patient die;
et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz, et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont, et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les II liiens a I spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers;	and the method of cutting or binding the limb is that you tie it above and below, and extend one minister with one bandage downward, and another minister with another bandage upward, and you separate the flesh between the two ties by one span wide until the bone is exposed;
puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part I drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain, et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	Then cut where the sore is, and place a piece of linen on each side, so that the cloth does not touch the healthy skin, and do not cause another injury or abscess to the patient.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment, ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans;	And if bleeding occurs while you are working, cauterize the area quickly or apply some hemostatic powders;
puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie, puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	then return to your treatment until it is complete, then bind the injured limb with an appropriate bandage, and care for it until it is healed;
et je te conterai k’il avint a I home en som piet:	and I will tell you what happened to a man in such a case:
il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu, et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet;	a black sore appeared that seemed burnt by fire, and this corruption started on his heel of the foot, spreading to cover the entire foot;
et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez;	and when the lord saw the corruption, he hastened to cut off the foot, and was healed;
et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi, et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions;	and after a long time the corruption returned to his thumb, and he came to me, and I put on him things that were repercussive after the purification of the body, and could not stop the corruptions;
et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere;	and he wanted me to cut off his hand, but I did not want to, as I had hope of repercussing the matter;
et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist, car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible;	and I also feared that if I cut his hand, he would die, because the man's vitality was weak;
et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre, et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez;	and he completely despaired and returned to his land, and hastened to cut off his hand, and was healed;
et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	and I have no use for it except for when one does something different with it, if there is need for it.
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe;	Sometimes an abscess appears in the flesh and remains so long that it causes a large accumulation of pus;
et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz;	and then it bursts and opens, and the pus flows out, leaving behind a cavity, just like a vessel;
et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com I drapelz deliiez, et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain», et n’est mie apelee «fistule»;	and the skin above it is as delicate as fine linen, and does not extend to the bone, nor to the nerve, and such a condition is called "sinus," and is not called "fistula";
mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»;	but if it extends so far that it reaches the bone deeply, then it is called "fistula";
et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz;	And take the skin so you cut around that skin entirely, and similarly when it is thin, as a cloth;
et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	and it does not matter for its decay.
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont, et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi:	And if you trust that the skin adheres, and the decay is not perfect, and the skin is thick with flesh, treat it by enema thus:
regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor, adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite:	check if the breast is swollen, and the pus that comes from it has a foul odor, then administer an Egyptian medicine enema which is made thus:
prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en I vassel au feu, tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel;	take pitch, oil, and litharge, equally, and put it in a vessel over the fire until the medicine turns red and becomes as thick as honey;
et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel, et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus;	and then take what you need of them, and make it into water and honey, and administer it as an enema, and hold the passage;
et laisse la medicine ens par II houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant;	and leave the medicine in for two hours, then remove it by squeezing;
fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor;	do this multiple times until the breast is cleansed, and the pus is removed;
et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres, quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus, puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez;	and sometimes an enema of ash water is given when this medicine is not present; take ashes from vine wood, pour water over it, then strain it and use it as an enema until you know the breast is well cleansed;
et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres, si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet;	and if the patient cannot tolerate it, neither the Egyptian medicine nor the ash water, then give an enema of water and honey with a little litharge ground up;
ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver, et li vins fait aerdre le sain;	When you make the enema of honey and mixed wine, let the honey have the property of cleansing and washing, and the wine soften the flesh;
et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez, si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li, et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin;	and when you have done this, and you are confident that the area is well cleansed, then use an enema to promote tissue growth, and prepare a diaphoretic poultice, which is made with rose oil in wine;
ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens;	when you administer enemas and ointments, of which I have described the properties in treating ointments;
et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer, si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein, ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez;	and if the opening of the area is small and the tube for the enema cannot enter, widen it with a probe slightly, and place a poultice made from Egyptian ointment or basilicon ointment until it is widened;
et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement I leu ou li clistere puisse entrer, et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	And if the wound is too wide, then sew it up leaving only enough space for a cloth dressing to enter, and if the opening that discharges pus is above, cut it lower down.
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char;	For when the pus is abundant, do not allow flesh to regenerate within it;
et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est, car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si apareille en teil maniere:	and if you cannot cut below the swelling as you wish, prepare it in such a way that the pus flows to the lowest point, for when the pus is abundant, do not allow flesh to regenerate within it, and if you cannot cut below the swelling as you wish, then prepare it in this manner:
que li bowe corre legierement aval, et n’i lassier rien de la bowe;	so that the pus flows gently downward, and do not leave any of the pus behind;
et pren medicines consolidatives por mettre sor le sain, et estent sus I drapeil de lin que cuevre tout le sain;	and take medicinal remedies to apply over the wound, and place on it a piece of linen that covers the entire wound;
puis cope as forces endroit le pertus dou sein I poc plus large dou premier, pues estent oignement souef sus I autre drapel selonc la quantiteit dou pertus, et le met sus le pertus dou sain por aligier la bowe, et n’oster mie le grant drapeil fuers que aprés maint jor une fois;	then cut in the appropriate places an opening larger than the first one, then apply ointment underneath another piece of cloth according to the size of the opening, and place it over the wound to alleviate the pain, and do not remove the large piece of linen until after several days once;
et celui qui est sor le pertus dou sein, oste sovent por oster la bowe, et saiches ceu que corra de la bowe, se c’est venin ou poc ou assez, ou digeste, ou indigeste;	and that which is over the opening of the wound, remove frequently to relieve the pain, and check what comes out of the wound, whether it is poison or too much or enough, or digestible, or undigested;
et pren warde se li patiens sent dolor ou nom, et s’il i a aposteme ou non, et quant ta medicine s’est en teil maniere estendue et tu vois la nature que saut sus le pertus dou sain, si saiches que li seins s’aert ja, et aproche li santez;	and take care if the patient feels pain or not, and whether there is an abscess or not, and when your medicine has been applied in such a manner and you see the nature of what comes out through the wound opening, know that the body is healing, and approach the treatment accordingly;
et puis le deslie le matin, ou le tier jor, et quant tu delies la plaie, si chainge I autre drapeil, et renovele l’oignement.	And then untie it in the morning, or on the third day, and when you untie the wound, change the cloth, and renew the ointment.
Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	And if the stomach throws up undigested food after many days, know that the stomach does not settle.
Et se venins subtilz cort aprés lonc tens, si ne te desperer mie de la santeit, car li santez aproche.	And if subtle symptoms appear after a long time, do not despair of health, for health is approaching.
Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire;	For there are people who suffer delays in flesh remedies for their wounds, and those who do the opposite;
et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie;	and if undigested food stays in the chest after many days, know that the chest does not clear itself;
et se li seins tarde d’aerdre, et est porloigniez, si ajoste medicines sechans moistes en substance et seches en vertut, si com oignement diafinit, car il i a grant partie de vitriole, et c’est li derriene medicine;	and if the chest is slow to clear and is prolonged, add drying but moist medicines in substance and dry in virtue, such as diaphoretic ointment, for it contains much vitriol, and this is the final medicine;
pren oignement dyafinit, et le font avec oile roset, et l’arose de viel vin igal en substance;	take diaphoretic ointment, and make it with rose oil, and dilute it equally with old wine;
puis le confit et en use;	then apply the ointment and use it;
et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez, quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens, ou tu pren mirre et aloen et encens, et le broie, et le poudre sus le miel quant il est sor le feu;	and this same thing cooks better when it thickens, when there is no definitive ointment present, take mummy wax, aloe, and incense, grind them together, and powder them over the honey while it is on the fire;
et puis en glue I drapel, et l’estent sor le sein, et aucune fois i aministre on aristologe longe, et racines de lis celeste, qui est ausi com farine de veces et centoire;	and then attach the piece of cloth to it and place it over the chest, and sometimes administer an aromatic herb called aristology longa, and roots of celestial lilies, which are similar to orache flour and centaury;
et en use de simples ou de compostes:	and use simple or compound remedies:
broie les, et en fai poudre, et met sus le miel que j’ai dit, et en use;	grind them and make powder, and mix it with the honey that I mentioned, and use it;
et se li cure est alongie, et n’est curez par ceste cure, adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l’os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens;	And if the treatment is prolonged and is not cured by this treatment, then you know that the corruption has reached deep into the bone, or affects hard members, or ligaments;
si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	if the treatment of the fistula is as we have said before.
de l’aposteme de l’ungle	of the abscess of the nail
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main, ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois;	Panarisis is an abscess that arises beneath the nail of the finger or toe, or occasionally occurs in other joints;
et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient I aposteme chaus, et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute;	and when it is old and no attention is given to it, then the abscess becomes severe, and spreads and discharges pus until it reaches the root of the nail, and may eventually spread completely;
et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	and the corrosion reaches the bone, causing severe pain, and the nail of the finger becomes swollen, and the color changes.
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle, puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	When you treat it as we have said in the section, and the treatment does not help, then it is necessary to cut away all the excess that remains from the nail, then cauterize the wound afterward.
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne;	The cauterization is a great aid if the bone is sound, and the nail is healthy;
et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece, si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char, et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement, et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout;	and if the nail adheres to the flesh and begins to pierce it, and bleeds, then you must place a thin strip of cloth under the nail where it penetrates the flesh, raise it up, and carefully and gently cut away that part of the flesh, and apply hot and corrosive medicines to remove everything;
puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	then cure it with ointments until it is healed.
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner;	And if the corruption is in the bone, then cut it out, and draw forth pus, for as long as corrupted bone remains, it cannot heal;
et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en I des nous si com il est devant dit, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	And if you see the toe corrupted, cut it at I of us as was said before, then treat it until it is healthy;
et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier;	And if he is wounded, and punctured, and feels great pain, then you must treat him first;
puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus, et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor;	Then cut the nail of the thumb diagonally from above, and be careful not to cut into the flesh below the nail, for the patient would feel too much pain;
et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	And if it happens, place something on top that soothes.
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	the pain of the swelling of the hand
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus, et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle, et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	The second joint that is born in the hands of some men is entirely flesh, and sometimes it has bones, and at times there is a nail; and some of them are born at the root of the joint, where the origin is in some places.
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet, et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet;	Those who are born with a toenail deformation do not move it, and those who are born at the toe joint may move it by chance;
la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere:	The body of one who is fleshy is so light, in such a manner:
taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	cut it at its root with a broad spatula.
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer:	Those who are born with issues at the root of the joint are difficult to treat:
si te tien dou coper.	so handle it gently.
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os, puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	In the one who is born or should be at the back door, it is necessary that you cut first the flesh roundly until the bone, then cut the bone to a suitable thickness for him, then treat it until it is healed.
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	The swelling that comes to both together comes by birth, or by the healing of a wound, or by burning with fire, or by similar things.
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz;	You must cut that union so that the parts repair according to their natural forms;
puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent;	then place between two cloths or damp cloths in rose oil, so that they do not rejoin;
ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	or place between two pieces of fine cloth until the wound is sealed as needed.
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	If swelling comes to either of his two hands with the palm, cut that swelling as it should be done.
des vils	of worms
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors;	The veins are thick, wrapped up, full of melancholic excesses, which come to many members of the body;
et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	and it happens more in the legs of those who walk and work and carry things, than in others.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	Therefore, you should administer enemas to him at times, and then treat him with the herb basil.
Li cure de fer si est selonc II manieres:	The iron treatment is according to two methods:
l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir;	one involves cutting them and drawing out the black blood;
et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	and the other method is that you open the vein and draw out all of it.
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere:	The treatment is according to this method:
arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez, puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil;	first raise the leg with hot water very strongly, until the thick blood is thinned, then extract the leg of the patient from above the thigh to below the knee;
puis cope la voinne en I leu, ou en II ou en III, d’une taille large, puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir;	Then cut the vein at I the place, or at II or at III, of a broad size, then lift and draw out black blood with your hand, from one side to the other, until as much blood comes out as the patient's strength can bear;
et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire;	and then bandage it, and instruct him to eat foods that promote black bile;
et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	and repeat the evacuation and bloodletting when the veins are full, as it benefits the patient.
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere:	The treatment is according to this manner:
reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil, puis le met ou bain, et li arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes;	raise the patient's leg if there is much hair, then place it in a bath, and wash the leg with hot water until it becomes red, and swell the veins;
et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville;	And if you do not have warm water, heat it by the fire, and then cut into the vein straight from the middle of the knee, or in the part above the ankle;
puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent;	Then work the skin to the bone, and strip the vein from each side until it appears when you feel it;
et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche;	and one sees it red and black, and when it enters the skin it appears like a white cord;
puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier, puis le cope en I autre leu ensus III dois;	then push the incision from behind, until it is raised from the skin, and then gently stretch it to the bone, then cut into another place three fingers above;
puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere, puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers;	then strip the skin over the vein until it appears, then lift it to the incision as you did before, and stretch it to another bone as you did previously;
puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet, puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille;	Then cut another length, or more if you need it, then lift it, and cut at the joint of the foot, then draw it out and lift it up to the second joint;
puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope;	then extract it joint by joint until it comes out completely, then cut it;
et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil fort double, et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz I rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse;	and if you cannot draw it out and lift it, pierce the thread with a strong double needle, then lift and draw it, and insert from underneath the edge, and turn your hand from side to side until it comes out;
et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide;	and be careful that it does not break, for if it breaks, it cannot be drawn out or lifted, and this causes harm to the patient;
et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset;	and when you have treated it all, place lamb's wool moistened in wine and rose oil over the wound site;
et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and treat it until it is healed.
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit, si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie;	And if the vein is constricted and twisted and wrapped together, and it is not straight as we have said, then you must cut it quickly, but do not sever it;
et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	and treat it as we have said before.
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne;	The form of the iron used to cut the vein is curved, and it does not cut but rather divides the vein;
et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	and it is of a broad curve, for if it were fine, it would cut the vein, but it should be thick as we have said, and here is its form:
de la voinne civile	of the civil vein
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor;	This vein is located in the legs, in warm parts where no herbs or trees grow, and in soil where there is no moisture;
et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir, si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	and by chance it may arise in other places than the legs, and this happens from the putrefaction that comes beneath the skin, as it enters the body like serpents and worms, arising between the skin and flesh.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation, puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	And if the signs of the beginning of this vein are such that there comes a very large inflammation in the leg, then the place changes, and the vein begins to come out, as if it were the root of a plant.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a II З., et la noe, et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe;	When the wound is open, it is necessary that you wrap around a piece of cloth from one and a half to two fingers' width, tie it securely, and let the cloth hang down the leg, and every time there is any looseness, wrap it tightly around the cloth and tie it.
et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue;	and if it is too long, cut off a part and wrap the remainder, but do not cut it at its base until it has fully emerged.
