Et comande au malaide k’il dorme sus son costeit sain, ou sus son dos.	And instruct the patient to sleep on their healthy side or on their back.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si n’i tochier, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et met sus ceu que nos avons devant dit;	And if hot abscesses come up, do not touch them, until the hot abscesses are calmed, and then apply what we have said before;
et puis revien a la restauration, et l’estraint si com il covient, s’il n’i a nul mavais accident;	and then return to the restoration, and bind it as is appropriate, if there is no adverse effect;
et c’est li maniere.	And this is the manner.
de la brisure de l’ajutoire	of the fracture of the shoulder
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des II manieres:	The shoulder joint is what is between the neck and the head of the shoulder, and if it is dislocated, one must restore it according to one of the two methods:
dont l’une est que tu pren I fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	one of which is that you take one rod filled with moistening material, according to this form:
Et lie as II chiés II liens, et les pent en haut, et siece li malaide sus I siege;	And tie the two ends with two ropes, and lift them up, and seat the patient on a chair;
puis li giete som bras brisiet sus le fust, tant qu’il viegne a l’aissele, et ait em mi une corbeure de fust, puis pent sus aucune pesant chose ou li ministres l’estende aval;	then place the dislocated arm over the rod, until it reaches the armpit, and have it form a curve on the rod, then lift it with some heavy object or have someone hold it down;
puis mette li mires la briseure igal a ses mains ensamble, tant que li briseure retorne si com il covient.	Then place the splint equal to his hands together, so that the splint returns as it should.
Et li autre maniere si est que on sovine le malaide sus son hatereil, et li lie la main a son col, puis comande a II ministres que li uns teigne ceu qui est sus la briseure a ses mains, et li autres teigne desoz a tout I liien, et estende chescuns a sa partie.	And the other method is that you lift the patient onto his back, and tie the hand to his neck, then instruct two assistants that one pull what is above the fracture with both hands, and the other pull below at the joint, each stretching their part.
Et se tu vues que li estraction soit plus fors, si estraint I liien desoz la briseure, et sus la briseure, et estende chescuns des ministres a sa part.	And if you wish that the extraction be stronger, then remove the ligament below the fracture, and above the fracture, and extend each of the tendons on its side.
Et se li briseure est prochiene au chief de l’espaule, si covient que tu mettes I liien moien desoz l’assele, et I autre vers lou coute, desoz la briseure;	And if the splint is close to the top of the shoulder, then you should place one band beneath the armpit, and the other towards the side, beneath the splint;
et ausi se li briseure est devers lou coute, si i covient mettre I liien legierement, sens labor, tant que li briseure soit igalz sus lou leu, et sus lou coute;	and likewise if the splint is towards the side, then place one band lightly, without strain, so that the splint remains equal on its place, and at the side;
puis met igal la brisure, si com il covient, et l’estraint, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	Then place the splint equally as it should be, and secure it, unless abscesses occur.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si ne l’estraindre mie jusc’a VII jors, et met sus lainne moillie en aisil et en oile roset, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez;	And if abscesses occur, do not secure it until the seventh day, and place linen soaked in oil and rose oil, until the abscesses are appeased;
puis l’estraint, et li maniere de l’estraindre si est que tu mettes l’emplaustre sus la briseure, puis assemble le bras sus l’ajutoire, et met ta main sus l’espaule ou sus lou sein;	Then it is restrained, and the way to restrain it is to place the plaster on the fracture, then bring the arm up to the shoulder, and put your hand on the shoulder or the chest;
et met le drapeil, et estraint sus l’ajutoire, et sus lou bras, si que li bras soit en leu d’esteles, s’aucune chose ne le te deffent, ou se li os n’est muez.	and apply the bandage, and restrain it on the shoulder, and on the arm, so that the arm is in a stable position, unless something prevents it, or if the bone has moved.
Et se tu doutes que li os ne se mueve, si use d’esteles, et met sus la brisure une estele plus large et plus fort des autres, et ait entre chescune estele I doi d’espaice, et soit chescune estele si grans qu’elle passe la briseure III dois de chescune part;	And if you doubt that the bone will move, use splints, and place on the fracture one splint wider and stronger than the others, and have between each splint a space of two fingers, and let each splint be so large that it passes the fracture three fingers on each side;
puis estrain sus les esteles, ensi com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre sus la briseure, plus fort et moins en aloignant.	Then pull up on the stars, as I said at the beginning of the chapter about fractures, more forcefully and less in pulling apart.
Et se tu vois l’assise des esteles, et l’estrignement, si com nos avons dit, en l’oure que tu restoures le membre brisiet, et tu doutes l’aposteme chaut, si le laisse a liier jusc’a septime jor, si com nos avons dit;	And if you see the setting of the bones and the compression, as we have said, when you are restoring the broken limb, and you fear a hot abscess, then leave it bound until the seventh day, as we have said;
puis regarde chescuns III jors lou lien, que prurite ne enfleure n’i viegne au leu, ou li norrissemens ne puist venir au membre por ceu k’il est trop estrois.	then check the bandage every three days to ensure that itching or swelling does not occur at the site, where the healing cannot reach the limb because it is too tight.
Si l’adrece, si com nos avons dit.	If it is reduced, as we have said.
Et se nulz telz accidens n’i vient, si ne lou desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou plus, et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ait ses mains sus son stomac;	And if no such accidents occur, do not loosen it before three days or more, and have the patient sleep on their back, with their hands on their stomach;
et met desoz l’ajutoire I cussin plain de laine igalment, et regarde chescune houre dou jor ou de la nut, que li figure dou membre brisiet ne se mueve, ou ne soit amollis li liiens;	and place under the shoulder a cushion filled evenly with wool, and observe every hour of day or night that the figure of the broken limb does not move, nor be softened the ligaments;
si l’adrece par la vertu de medicine, et li done la viande que nos avons devant mis, en teil maniere que li viande soit au premier subtilz;	and if it is addressed by the virtue of medicine, and give him the meat that we mentioned before, in such a way that the meat is at first finely prepared;
et quant il comance a reprendre, si soit grosse.	and when he begins to recover, it should be more substantial.
Et est costume que li ajutoire et li jambe doient estre repris en XL jors dou tout;	And it is customary that the shoulder and the leg should be treated for forty days in total;
et adonques lou doit on desliier et aministrer bain et medicines d’oignemens por le leu adrecier.	and then it must be loosened and administered baths and ointment medicines to heal the area;
Et se li estricture est laide et emboee, si demore a desliier L jors ou II mois.	And if the constriction is tight and stuck, then wait one day or two months.
de la brisure du bras	of the fracture of the arm
Li bras est compos de II os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet;	The arm is composed of two bones, which are called the two "humerus", of which one is small, and it is the one that contains the socket;
et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi;	and the other is large, and it is the one that is below, towards the little finger;
par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	by chance, only the large humerus may be broken, or the small one, and by chance both together.
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations;	When the small humerus is broken, the restoration is easy, and the healing;
et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble.	and when the large one is broken, the healing is difficult, and more troublesome than when both are broken together.
Se c’est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.	If it is the small phalanx that is merely broken, then it must be gently extended and placed evenly.
Et se c’est li grans foscile, si le covient estraindre plus fort;	And if it is the large abscess, then it must be squeezed more forcefully;
et l’estende sus I cussin, et teigne le pouchet de la main plus haut des autres, et li petis dois plus bas des autres dois, et soit li malaides croisiez sus lui meisme, et I cussin devant lui plus haut, que li malaides ne soffre nule labor;	and lay it out on a cushion, and tie the poultice higher than the others, and place the smaller one lower than the other two, and let the patient lie crossed upon himself, and have the cushion in front of him raised, so that the patient does not suffer any labor.
puis estende li ministres som bras a la partie desoz a sa main, ou a I liien, et uns autres ministres a I autre au desus.	then extend the assistants' arms to the side of his hand, or at the joint, and another assistant on the other side above.
Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	And then place the patient evenly, according to his best form.
Et se en la brisure a pieces, si met chescune en son leu, et s’il en i a nule desevree ke poigne lou keur, et tu ne la pues restorer en son leu, si fent sus et l’oste, si com nos avons dit devant.	And if there are multiple fractures, place each piece in its proper position, and if any are displaced causing pain to the heart, and you cannot restore it to its proper position, then cut it out as we have said before.
Et se avec la briseure a plaie, je en ai parleit au chapistre singuler;	And if with the instrument for wounds, I have spoken about it in the separate chapter;
si pren la cure.	then take the treatment.
Et se en l’encomencement dou restorement sorvient apostemes chaus, si glue I drapeil de cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire blainche, que ne soit mie ne trop durs ne trop molz;	And if in the beginning of the restoration abscesses occur, then apply a bandage made of rose oil and white wax that is neither too hard nor too soft;
et lie I drapeil par sus subtilment, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez.	and apply the bandage gently, until the warm abscess is relieved.
Et puis oste lou cerote, et i met l’emplaustre de la poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, pues met les esteles, et soit li estele de la briseure adés plus fors, et un poc plus large que les autres;	And then remove the wax and apply a poultice of ground powder with plenty of egg, and place the plasters, with the one from the fracture being slightly thicker and wider than the others;
et saiches que il doit avoir VI esteles ou bras em plusors dispositions:	and note that there should be six plasters on the arm in various positions:
soit que li briseure soit en l’un des os, soit en II;	whether the fracture is in one bone or in two;
et estraint plus sus la briseure que autre part, et toz jors moins en aloignant, si com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre;	and hold it tighter near the break than elsewhere, and gradually less as you move away, as I said at the beginning of the chapter;
et soient li drapelz que sont sus la briseure molz et moistes, et ne soient mie dur ne aspres;	and let the dressings that are on the break be soft and moist, and not hard or rough;
et soit li filz, dont il est estrains, de lin, ne trop gros ne trop menus, si com nos avons dit.	and let the thread, of which it is made, be linen, neither too thick nor too thin, as we have said.
Et rewarde lou membre et lou liien aprés aucuns jors.	And examine the limb and its joint after several days.
Et se aucuns mavais accidens vient au membre, si com prurite ki vient au membre, si covient que tu aroses lou membre d’aigue chaude, tant que cil prurites soit apaisiez;	And if any bad incident occurs to the limb, such as itching that comes to the limb, then you should rinse the limb with hot water until the itching is relieved;
et laisse le membre ne mie estroit reposer.	and let the limb rest without being confined tightly.
Et puis rencomence l’estrignement, et se li liiens est amolis et li os desevrez, et semblant chose, si l’adresce.	And then resume the compression, and if the joint is weakened and the bone dislocated, or similar things, address them.
Et se pren warde se li norrissemens ne puet venir au membre, por ceu qu’il est trop estrois, si covient que tu l’amollisses I poc, et laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant que li norrissemens i corre, et puis l’estraint.	And be careful if the swelling cannot reach the limb because it is too tight, then you should loosen it a bit, and leave it like this for several days until the swelling can flow, and then compress it.
Et se nules de ces choses que nos avons dit ne vient au malaide, si ne lou desliier jusc’a XX jors.	And if none of these things we have said come to the patient, do not loosen them until twenty days have passed.
ou enqui entor, puis li pent les mains a son col, et soit ses cols igalz, et se warde de movement et de degitement, et dorme sus son dos;	When examining around, then place his hands on his neck, and let his necks be even, and beware of movement and shaking, and sleep on his back;
et saiches que ceste briseure est restoree en XXX jors ou en XXXV, et par aventure en XX jors, selonc les compositions et les complexions des vertus.	and know that this fracture is restored in thirty days or in thirty-five, and sometimes in twenty days, according to the compositions and the strengths of the constitutions.
de la brisure de la main	Of the fracture of the hand
Saiches que au dos de la main et as nous des dois avient poc de briseures, et n’i vient mais que ploieure maintes fois.	Know that on the back of the hand and on both sides there are few fractures, and it rarely happens but many sprains occur.
Et quant li plante de la main est brisie ou ploie, si covient que li malaides siece croisiet, et siet droitement devant lui igalement;	And when the palm of the hand is broken or bent, it is necessary that the patient sits cross-legged and sits squarely facing forward;
puis met sa main sus la toie estendue, et estende li ministres les os brisiez, et les mete igalz li mires, tant qu’il soient bien joint;	then place his hand on the extended cloth, and the attendants extend the broken bones, and make them even the marrow, until they are well joined;
et met l’emplastre et les estoupes, se apostemes n’i vient, puis i met une estele selonc la quantiteit dou leu;	and apply the plaster and bandages, if no abscess forms, then place a splint according to the size of the area;
et soit envoloupee en I drapeil de lin.	and wrap it in a piece of linen cloth.
Et se li briseure est au pardedens entor lou ventre de la plante, si fai une spere de drapelz, et comande au malaide qu’il l’estrigne a sa plante brisie;	And if the fracture is on the inner side near the base of the foot, make a pad of cloth and instruct the patient to bind it to their fractured foot;
et puis l’estrain d’un lonc drapeil, et soit li estele de keur souef ausi grans com li plante de la main, et l’estraint, si com il covient.	and then wrap it with a long piece of cloth, and make the splint as thick as the palm of the hand, and bind it securely as required.
Et se li brisure est au defuer, si covient que tu mettes une estele sus, et une autre desoz en la plante, si que li mains soit overte et droite, puis le lie tot entor la main, et estanche lou liien entre les dois.	And if the fracture is on the side, then you must place one pad above and another below the sole of the foot, so that the hand is open and straight, then bandage it quickly around the hand, and secure the binding between the two pads.
Et se li briseure vient a aucun des nous des dois, se c’est li pouchés, si le met igal, si com il covient;	And if the fracture occurs at one of the bones on either side, and it is a comminuted fracture, set it evenly as required;
et l’estraint avec la plante, et se tu vues si met une estele droite petite por lever la briseure, et ne se mueve;	and you press it with the palm, and if you wish place a small straight splinter to lift the fracture, and it does not move;
et se li brisure est as autres dois, si com en l’indice ou l’un des autres, si le met igal, et lou lie avec lou doi sain qui est aprés;	and if the fracture is in either of the other two, such as in the index finger or one of the others, align it equally, and bind it with the healthy finger next to it;
ou tu les lie toz en I tenant, que mues vaut, ou tu met sus une estele, si com ou pouchet;	tie them all together so that movement is prevented, or place a splinter on them, like in a bandage;
et pren warde en la restauration et en la disposition d’aposteme chaut, et secor ceu qui i vient, si com j’ai dit.	and be careful in the restoration and disposition of a hot abscess, and support those who come to it, as I have said.
de la cuixe brisie	of a broken thigh
Li os de la cuixe est maintes fois brisiez, et bien le voit on quant elle torne devant et derrier;	The bone of the thigh is often fractured, and it is well seen when it turns forward and backward;
et li restauration si est c’on lie I liien desus la briseure, et I autre desoz.	And the restoration is such that one binds a bandage above the fracture, and another below.
Et li malaides gise sus sa faice, puis estende chescuns ministres son lien a sa part igalment;	And the patient lies on their back, then each attendant extends their bandage equally on their side;
et c’est quant li brisure est emmi l’os.	and this is when the fracture is in the bone.
Et se li brisure est prochiene a la racine de la cuixe, si soit li uns des liiens devers lou poignil, et li autres liiens desoz la briseure.	And if the break is near the root of the thigh, then one bandage should be towards the hip, and the other bandages below the break.
Et ausi s’elle est prochiene au genoil, et adonques soit li liens delez lou genoil, et soit li extension aval;	And if it is near the knee, then the bandages should be near the knee, and the extension below;
puis mette li mires l’os igal a ses II mains, tant qu’il soit selonc sa figure natureil, et puis met l’emplaustre, et lou lie, se apostemes chaz n’i vient.	then the physician should align the bone equally with both hands, so that it is according to its natural position, and then apply a plaster, and bind it, unless abscesses occur.
Et s’il i a aposteme chaut, si le laisse apaisier puis revien a ton ovraige et a ta cure;	And if there is a hot abscess, let it subside before returning to your work and treatment;
li lieure est faite en teil maniere.	the ligature is made in such a manner.
Il covient que tu envoloupes sus la briseure I bendeil dur doublé en II ou III, et en demoure li superfluitez, puis torne la jambe tant que li talons veigne a la racine de la naige, et boute I fil lonc entre la cuixe et la jambe, delez lou genoil desoz, et veignent li chief dou fil au desus;	You must wrap around the fracture one bandage thickly in two or three layers, and remove any excess, then position the leg so that the heels align with the root of the thigh, and insert a long thread between the thigh and the leg near the knee underneath, with the ends of the thread above.
puis torne sus la jambe et sus la cuixe le bendeil, puis met sus la briseure esteles, et met une estele sus l’os de la jambe;	then wrap the bandage around the leg and thigh, then place splints on the fracture, and put a splint on the bone of the leg;
puis emple le leu vuit entre la jambe et la cuixe de drapelz souef por mettre igal l’estrignement, puis comence a liier forment III tors ou IIII sus la briseure;	Then place a cloth between the thigh and the calf to make the compression even, then begin binding tightly three times or four above the fracture;
et quant plus vas en sus de la briseure, et moins l’estraint;	and as you go further up from the fracture, the binding is less tight;
puis enten as II chiés dou fil que tu as bouteit entre la jambe et la cuixe, et en lie III esteles que sont desus, puis revai au desoz au chief dou fil, tant que tu veignes delez le piet;	then tighten the two threads you placed between the thigh and the calf, and bind three bands above them, then go back behind to the head of the thread until you reach the foot;
et l’estraint, si qu’il ne se mueve de son leu, puis le laisse ensi, puis k’il n’i vient ne aposteme ne enfleure n’autre semblant.	and bind it so that it does not move from its place, then leave it thus, so that no abscess or swelling occurs.
Et s’il i avient, si le deslie, et adresce ceu que i vient, si com nos avons dit maintes fois;	And if it does occur, loosen it and address what happens, as we have said many times;
et se il i a pieces de l’os que poigne, si le covient ewer, s’om puet;	and if there are fragments of bone that cause pain, they must be removed, if possible;
et s’on ne puet, si covient fendre le leu, et traire fuer;	and if it cannot be done, then it is necessary to cut the area and extract the contents;
et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant k’il soit sanez.	and treat it as we have said, until it is healed.
Et aucune fois est brisie li cuixe ensi c’on i met esteles, si com en l’ajutoire et ou bras;	And sometimes the thigh is broken in such a way that splints must be applied, as with the shoulder and arm;
toutevoie, en la restauration ensi faite ne cloche mie li malaides.	nevertheless, in this manner of restoration, the patient does no harm.
Et saiches que li cuixe est restoree en L jors, ou poc moins ou poc plus, selonc les diversitez des complexions.	And know that the thigh is restored in 21 days, or a few less or more, according to the differences in temperaments.
de la ruelle dou genoil	of the knee joint
Saiches que en la ruelle dou genoil avient poc brisure, mais elle ploie maintes fois.	Know that in the joint of the knee there is frequent bruising, but it bends many times.
Et s’elle brise, si n’est mais c’une fendure, ou I pertus, et avient a tout plaie, et sens plaie, et ce sent om bien.	And if it breaks, it is only a crack, or an aperture, and it becomes like any wound, and feels as a wound, and this people feel well.
Et li restauration si est c’on mette igal ceu qui est rons a ses dois, tant qu’il soit assemblez mues c’on puet;	And the restoration is such that one sets equal the toes which are bent at their joints, until they are aligned as much as possible;
puis met l’emplaustre, et i met une estele reonde, se tu en as mestier, et l’estraint si com il covient, puis rewarde toutes les dispositions que nos avons dit ens autres briseures, si com aposteme chaut et autre semblant;	Then apply the plaster, and if needed, place a round splinter, and secure it as appropriate, then review all the arrangements we have mentioned for other fractures, such as hot abscesses and similar conditions;
si met a chescun accident ceu k’il li covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then apply to each injury what is appropriate for it until he is healed.
de la brisure de la jambe	Of the breaking of the leg
Saiches que en la jambe ait II os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»;	Know that in the leg there are two bones, one of which is properly called "mustelz," and the other is called "foscile";
et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i. Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.	and any other type of fracture that occurs in the arm is treated similarly to the leg, and the treatment is the same as for the arm. And if both bones are broken together, then treat the leg from all sides.
Et se li os subtilz est brisiez, si torne devant.	And if the finer bone is broken, then turn it forward.
Et se li gros os est brisiez, si sent on grant dolor, et le voit on bien;	And if the large bone is broken, one feels great pain, and it is clearly visible;
et torne desoz.	and turn away from it.
Adonques amenistre extension, et le met igal, et lie les esteles igalement;	Then treat with extension, and place it evenly, and bind the splints equally;
mais toutevoie, il covient se li brisure est laide, et il i a plusors pieces, que li extension soit menor et plus legiere;	but still, if the break is severe and there are many pieces, the extension should be gentler and lighter;
et l’alige selonc ta vertu.	and apply it according to your skill.
Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, si pren II faixes de fust chevees que porpreignent la jambe d’une part et d’autre, et soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz;	And when you have completed your work, take two strips of wood that will support the leg from both sides, and let them run along the length of the leg from the knee down;
puis envoloupe en II leus I bendeil desus et desoz, et le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, et ensi est bien;	Then wrap with two layers one bandage above and below, and place it in the middle as well, so that at this point the leg cannot turn to either side, and thus it is secure;
et aucun i aministrent I bers dou lonc de la jambe, et s’est de fust, et i met on la jambe por warder de movement, et proprement fait on ceu en la brisure ou il a plaie;	and some apply one board along the length of the leg, and if it is wooden, they place it on the leg to prevent movement, and properly this is done in fractures where there is an open wound;
et remue chescun jor la jambe, por veoir s’il i a aposteme chaut n’autre accident;	and move the leg each day to check for an abscess or other complications;
si le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	treat it until it is healed.
de la brisure des os dou piet	of the fracture of the foot bones
A la cheville ne vient point de brisure, mais as os dou piet vient aucune fois brisure et as dois poc, et n’i avient fuer que quassure em plusor dispositions.	At the ankle there is no fracture, but sometimes a fracture occurs in the bones of the foot and at the two joints, and it happens that it breaks in many conditions.
Et s’il avient as os dou piet brisure, et tu vois ces os sormonter l’un l’autre, si mette si malaides som piet sus la terre, ausi com s’il voloit aler, et puis met maintenant ton piet sus lou sien, lai ou li os sont levez, puis le presse tant k’il reveignent en lor leus;	And if a fracture occurs in the bones of the foot, and you see these bones protrude one over the other, place the patient's foot on the ground as if they were going to walk, then now put your foot on top of theirs where the bones are raised, and then press so that they return to their places;
puis met l’emplaustre et estoupes sus, et met desoz lou ventre dou piet une petite tauble a II chiés plains, puis l’estraint au piet avenanment, puis que tu as envoloupez drapelz entor, et autres choses dont tu as mestier.	Then apply the plaster and plugs over it, and place under the belly of the foot a small tablet filled with two spoonfuls, then bind it tightly to the foot after wrapping it with cloths, and other things that you need.
Et quant III jors ou IIII seront passez, si deslie lou liien, car tu troveras les os igalz, soient brisiez, soient desaluez.	And when three or four days have passed, loosen the bandage, for you will find the bones even, whether they are broken or dislocated.
Et s’il i a aucuns des dois brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit as dois de la main;	And if any of the two is broken, restore them as we have said about those of the hand;
puis met au doi brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou doi, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j’ai dit, et l’estrain avenanment;	Then place a splint on the broken toe according to its length, and make it slightly wider, then place under the foot the tablet that I mentioned, and bind it tightly;
et s’il en i a II ou III, ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun doi une estele selonc sa quantiteit, envoloupee en I drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet;	and if there are two or three, or more, broken toes, place a splint on each toe according to its size, wrapped in one piece of linen cloth, and bind the tablet under the foot;
et soit estans sus lou chief de la tauble defuer lou ventre dou piet, si qu’il le teigne bien.	and let them stand on top of the table to expose the belly of the thigh, so that it is well covered.
Et covient que tu n’oblier mie les autres choses que j’ai dit as autres briseures, des que nos avons dit;	And you must not forget the other things that I said to the other surgeons, as we have mentioned;
et secor chescun accident si com il covient.	and attend to each incident as is appropriate.
de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	of the fracture of the bone of the finger
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier;	When the bone of the woman's pelvis is broken, make her sit with her legs apart, then incline her towards the part of the back, and hold her from behind;
puis emplisse li baile la nature de la malaide de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com I sto;	then fill the area of the woman's pelvis with cotton, and place in it as much as fits;
puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto;	then help the woman stand up, and lift her back little by little, and then push the cotton until it reaches the entrance of the pelvis, and return the bone with the padding;
et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice VII jors ou entor:	and when she wishes to urinate, remove the cotton, and when she has urinated, replace it, and thus do for seven days or thereabouts:
si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature;	the fracture will be restored, and if you wish, take a sheep's bladder, tie a tube to the opening, and insert the entire bladder into the body;
puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens:	then blow forcefully into the tube until the bladder is inflated inside:
la nature si revenra li brisure;	the body will return the fracture to its proper place;
puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit sanez.	then fill it with cotton and leave it this way for several days until it is healed.
Et quant li os dou poignil de l’ome est brisiez, ou de la femme, si le restoure ensi com nos avons dit en l’os de la hainche;	And when the bone of the thumb of a man or woman is broken, restore it as we have described for the hip bone;
et ne sont mie occultees ces briseures prochienes a celui qui i met son estude et son us, et entent mon livre.	And these nearby fractures are not hidden from one who puts his study and practice into it, and my book becomes clear.
Car li brisure li signifie em plusors dispositions la droite voie de la restauration:	For the fracture indicates in various positions the right way to restoration:
enten le donques.	Then understand it.
En la verge, quant elle est brisie, pren une gorge d’oie et i boute la verge;	In the shaft, when it is broken, take a goose neck and insert the shaft into it;
puis envoloupe drapelz entor, et le laisse III jors ou enqui entor, et il sera sanez hastanment.	then wrap cloths around it, and leave it for three days while wrapping around it, and it will heal quickly.
de brisure avec plaie	of fracture with wound
Il covient a celui qui a brisure avec plaie, meismement s’elle est grans, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire ou semblant, qu’il soit sainiez maintenant, si que les sainies que nos avons dit le tesmoignent.	It is necessary for one who has a fracture with a wound, especially if it is large, such as the bone of the thigh or shoulder or similar, to be treated now, so that the treatments we have mentioned bear witness.
Et se li plaie saine, si la restainche de vitriole, se tu n’as autre chose, puis rencomence a restorer la briseure en cele meisme houre, ou celui jor, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the wound heals, then staunch it with vitriol, if you have nothing else, and then restart the healing process at the same hour, or on that day, unless abscesses come.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si laisse la restauration jusc’a nuevime jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et n’i touchier ne au tier jor ne au quart, car tu i feroies venir malvais accident.	And if abscesses come, then leave the restoration until a new day, until the abscesses are appeased, and do not touch them on the third or fourth day, for you would cause a harmful accident.
Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.	And if the broken bone is apparent on the exposed chest, then it must be set gently with your hands, with slight extension.
Et se li extensions ne t’est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a VII dois ou VIII de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie;	And if the extension is not available to match your hands, then use this iron instrument which is seven or eight inches long, and the width is according to the size of the wound;
et por ceu est mestier au mire qu’il empreigne III ou IIII, selonc ceu qu’il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure;	and for this reason it is necessary for the physician to take III or IIII, according to what he needs for each treatment of fracture;
et soit rons et un poc gros, k’il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:	and let it be straight and somewhat thick, so that it does not bend under the pressure on the limb during your work, and sharp at the front, and thick from the middle forward, thus:
Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l’os apparent;	And it is called "palainche", for which it is necessary that the curved head be placed on the top of the visible bone;
et le boute a une fois, tant k’il reviegne, et soit igalz l’un encontre l’autre.	and push it in at once, until it fits, and let them be equal to each other.
Et se li brisure est subtilz, et li estrumens ne puet bien prendre l’os, si covient que tu copes lou chief de l’os, tant que li estrumens en ait possance.	And if the fracture is subtle, and the instrument cannot properly grasp the bone, then you must cut the head of the bone until the instrument can grip it.
Et se tu ne pues ramener l’os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope d’un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir;	And if you cannot return the bone as we have said, then cut off a piece with an appropriate instrument, such as a scalpel or saw, to your ability;
puis reis ceu qui est demorez en l’os d’aspreteit et de menues escorces.	Then raise the part that is stuck in the bone of hardness and small splinters.
Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil.	And when the bone is returned and the patient feels great pain afterwards, know that it is not in its natural place.
Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, puis moille I drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c’est en esteit;	Place it back in its proper place, then moisten the area with black styptic wine, and do this properly if it is necessary.
et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption;	and do not apply plaster or anything else with oil to the wound, as it may cause putrefaction and corruption;
puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l’os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure;	then administer bandages after you have restored the bone, and leave the wound uncovered, and cut the covering all around according to the size of the wound, and take care that the wound is not compressed with the fracture;
et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois;	and many times foolish doctors have done this, and it has led to the death or corruption of the patient;
et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	And let the compresses be softer and lower than for other fractures.
Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n’i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n’i covient mie mettre sus esteles;	And if the wound is bad or large, and you fear that some harm may occur, as we have said, and you find pain in the area, then you should not apply hot coals to it;
mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie.	but wrap it instead with hard cloths in place of hot coals, and bind them.
Et quant tu vois aprés I jor ou II enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.	And when you see after one or two days that the wound is producing pus, remove what you placed over it entirely, and put on healing salve, such as tetrahermion ointment and similar.
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre II fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.	And it is necessary to loosen the limb twice a day, in the morning and evening, until it is healed and sound.
Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	And the limb should be positioned in such a way that the pus flows down gently.
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	And if many days pass and it cannot heal but continues to produce pus, know that there are small pieces of bone, so you must probe the wound with a probe, and remove all these loose pieces that cause pain.
Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu’il dist en son chapistre ci devant.	And if a fistula comes to the place, or any other form of corruption, then it is necessary that you treat it, according to what he says in his chapter above.
Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant qu’il porrisse;	And when the bone is broken and protruding from the limb, such as the bone of the thigh or shoulder, and other similar cases involving large limbs, do not attempt to extract it, for many die in such attempts; instead, leave it until it becomes infected.
par aventure cherra par lui aprés XX jors ou XXX, puis cure la plaie, se tu pues;	by chance it will fall off after twenty days or thirty, then treat the wound if you can;
et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.	and if you cannot, leave it as it is.
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	of bruises that come upon the joint
Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre;	We often see this after the healing of the fracture, especially when it is near the joint, and it is a terrible thing to see the shape of the limb;
et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.	and by chance, the limb cannot perform its natural functions.
Pren warde donques se li nous est fres:	Take care then if the bone is fresh:
si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil;	if the wound is fresh, administer astringent medicines such as aloes, incense, and myrrh, and sarcocolle, acacia, and similar others; take any of these things or all together, and mix them with astringent wine or with egg whites or with olive oil;
et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors;	and place them on the knot with plugs, and bind tightly, and do not loosen it at any time;
et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee;	and then dislocate it, and start again with another one until the knot is removed;
ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite;	where you bind over a well-made piece of cloth;
car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu’il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres;	for the properties of the cloth are such that they remove all swellings from the limbs;
et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l’oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent;	and if the knot has already hardened like a stone and needs to be removed, then cover it with a cloth, and the excess will become apparent;
ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu’ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee.	where you refer it to a barber to remove it completely, and continue treating it until it is healed.
dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison	of the limb which is weak after recovery
Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes:	When the fracture of the bone is restored, and the limb remains weak and delicate afterwards, this happens for many reasons:
de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit;	one reason is that it was bound too tightly, and was not bound as it should have been;
ou por ceu qu’il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre;	or because there were too many bandages, and the limb could not properly undergo treatment;
ou por multitude d’arosement;	or due to excessive bleeding;
ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre;	or because of too much movement, not at the right time;
ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.	or because they have little blood in their body, so they are weak.
Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui;	And the treatment is that you should make the patient eat, and soften the body, until the blood is multiplied within him;
et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce;	and the minister bathes him, and gives him joy and ease;
puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l’arose sovent d’aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre;	then applies pitch to the limb, so that the pitch attracts the swelling, and frequently rinses it with cold water, until the swelling flows into the limb;
et reviegne a sa figure natureil.	and returns to its natural form.
dou membre tort aprés la santeit	of the limb twisted after the sickness
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil:	When the limb is twisted after restoration, and the bone is clearly broken, and the shape of the limb is ugly, it does not lose its natural function nonetheless:
si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre;	do not believe those fools who say that one should break the limb anew, and many foolish physicians have done this in our land;
et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors;	and these practices are blamed, and great harms come from them, and by chance death occurs;
toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses;	nevertheless, if the ligatures and tortures are fresh, they should be soaked in hot water, or herbs that soften should be boiled, such as leaves of mallows, roots, hawthorn, and similar things;
et li fai I emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus;	and apply a softening poultice, such as well-made mallow, and take the mucilage of mallows, and mix it with goose grease or sesame oil, and apply the poultice;
ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	or take fat figs and crush them with flaxseed, and similar medications that reduce swelling.
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes.	And sometimes the knot is removed to rub continuously and for a long time with wet hands.
Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	And let movement be administered to the limb every hour.
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement;	And if the tortuosity is swollen and hardened, like a stone, and it needs to be removed with iron, then it must be cut up to the bone, with a subtle incision lightly;
et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.	and apply compression and careful attention in the treatment.
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	Here begins the book of dislocations
Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	Dislocation occurs when a joint moves out of its place, which prevents it from moving, and the limb is misaligned, causing the patient great pain and injury.
Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.	When dislocation occurs to anyone, it is necessary now to return it without delay.
Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu;	For if one delays, the area swells, and by chance it may be reset with difficulty to its place;
por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez:	for it is not advisable to move it when it is swollen:
maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors;	often it causes spasms and other pains;
toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez;	still, when this happens, make the patient bleed, then leave them alone until the abscesses are resolved;
puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	Then raise the limb with hot water and oil, then reset it gently, and treat each member as the treatment will come into its place.
Et j’ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief jusc’a piez.	And I have arranged the chapters on dislocations from the head down to the feet.
des mandibules	of the jawbones
Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations d’ambedous est selonc II manieres:	It sometimes happens that the jaw joints are dislocated, and the dislocation of both is according to two methods:
ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc;	when they are slightly out of place and slightly loosened;
ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche qu’il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole.	or they are completely dislocated and hang towards the worse side, causing saliva to pour from the mouth which he cannot hold back, nor can he close his mouth, and wraps his tongue around the words.
Quant li dislocations est petite, si revient par li em plusors disposicions.	When the dislocation is small, it returns on its own in many cases.
Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie;	And if it is complete and perfect, then you must reset it quickly, and do not delay;
et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de II pars;	And in such a manner that the minister holds the head of the patient, and puts his thumb from one of his hands at the root of the dislocation of the jaw inside the mouth, if the dislocation is on both sides;
et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal;	and the other two hands should be withdrawn, to place equally;
et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	and instruct the patient to soften his jawbones and move them in all directions.
Et li mires la mete igal, tant qu’elle reveigne en son leu.	And the doctor should place it evenly, so that it returns to its place.
Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les II mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement;	And if resetting is difficult, especially if both jawbones are dislocated together, soak them in warm water and oil until they can be reset gently;
ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	do not delay in resetting it, as we have said.
Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens;	And when they are brought back evenly, and the mouth of the patient clots well to soften, then place moistened cloths in cerate made of rose oil and wax, then bind it gently with soft bandages;
et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre II cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules;	and let the patient sleep on his back, and his shoulders be placed between two cushions, so that he does not move to either side, nor tries to move, but take light food, until the pains are gone, and the jaws are bound;
et puis menjuce ce qu’il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie d’ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.	and then let him eat what he wants lightly, and do not work to open the mouth for eating and drinking, until the jaw is well bound and healed.
Et se les II mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.	And if the two mandibles cannot be reset perfectly in one hour, and are not returned to their places, it results in recurring fevers and habitual diarrhea, and possibly vomiting of bile.
Et quant tu verras ceu, adonc saiches que c’est perdicions;	And when you see this, then you know that it is a sign of impending danger;
et maintes fois muert cil cui il avient, en VIIII jors.	And many times the person who experiences this dies within nine days.
de la forcelle	of strength
Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	The joint cannot be dislocated from the side within the continuation of the ribs and the hip, and it is sometimes dislocated outward, and this is well felt.
Et li restauration si est que li malaides gise sovin sor son dos, et estende ses bras;	And the restoration is such that the patient lies supine on their back, and extends their arms;
et puis presse le leu forment a ta palme, et elle revenra;	and then press the area firmly with your palm, and it will return;
puis met sus l’emplaustre et lou bendeil, et l’estraint;	then apply the plaster and bandage, and secure it;
et li chiez qui est devers lou coute ne puet desaluer;	and the head that is near the side cannot be dislocated;
se poc non, et se il desalue aucune fois, si le ramoinne a son leu, si com nos avons dit;	if it does, and if it dislocates at any time, then reset it to its place, as we have said;
puis met sus l’emplaustre et le bendeil, et l’estraint, et coumande au malaide qu’il se repose tant qu’il soit sanez;	then apply the plaster and bandage, and secure it, and instruct the patient to rest until they are healed;
et ensi meisme est ramenez li chiés de l’espale, quant il est desevrez de son leu.	And similarly, the head of the spine is reset when it has come out of its place.
de la dislocation de l’espaule	of the dislocation of the shoulder
Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc III manieres:	Know that the shoulder is dislocated in no more than three ways:
de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz;	one of which is that it dislocates at the part of the socket on the inner side;
et li seconde est a la partie dou pis;	and the second is at the part of the bottom;
et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc;	and occasionally it dislocates at the top part, and this happens rarely;
et ne desalue mie derrier por l’espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners;	and it does not dislocate behind the shoulder, nor inward towards the nerves;
et plusors fois desalue desoz vers l’assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment;	and it often dislocates towards the socket on the inner side, especially for those with little flesh, because the shoulder is more prone to this among them;
a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.	For those who have enough flesh, it sticks with difficulty, and reenters with difficulty.
Et par aventure avient a aucuns homes percussion ou casseure, et enfle li espaule d’un aposteme chaut, et cuide qu’elle est desaluee par ceu.	And sometimes it happens to some men that there is a blow or fracture, and the shoulder swells with a hot abscess, and they believe that it is dislocated because of this.
Il covient donques que tu l’esprueves, tant que tu en soies certains;	It is necessary then that you test it until you are certain;
et adonques encomence la cure.	and then begin the treatment.
Et est conue li dislocations quant il est aval vers l’assele, et met difference entre l’espaule malade et la saine, et tu troveras entre lor diversiteit manifeste;	And dislocation is known when it is towards the armpit, and there is a difference between the affected shoulder and the healthy one, and you will find their difference evident;
et troveras au chief de l’espaule une fosse, et desoz l’assele au tochier le chief de l’espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes;	and you will find a depression at the top of the shoulder, and below the armpit towards the head of the shoulder, as if it were an eye;
et ne puet li malaides ramener sa main a son neis, ne movoir de nulz movemens;	and the patient cannot bring their hand to their nose, nor move in any way;
et ausi, s’elle est desaluee en haut, si n’est mie occultee, car tu le trueves manifestement au tochier;	And so, if it is reduced above, it is not hidden, for you find it clearly by palpation;
et ceste maniere de dislocation n’est mie fors a ramener, quant elle est novele, ou se li enfes est malaides.	And this type of dislocation is not to be reduced when it is new, or if the child is ill.
Et li maniere est que li ministres lieve la main dou malaide en haut, puis met tes peuchas desoz l’assele, et lieve la jointure a force en haut au leu;	And the method is that the practitioner lifts the patient's hand upwards, then places his fingers under the armpit, and raises the joint forcefully upwards to its place;
et li ministres lieve la main, et l’estende en haut, pues le mette desoz;	And the practitioner lifts the hand and extends it upwards, then places it underneath;
si venra hastanment.	it will come quickly.
Et s’elle ne vient si com nos avons dit em mains jors aprés, si covient ke li malaides soit baigniez en aigue chaude;	And if it does not come as we have said within several days, then it is necessary that the patient be bathed in hot water;
et li amenistre arosement mollifiant et assouajant, si com decoction de altee et de fenugrec et de mellilote en aigue, et soit amenistree;	and the healer uses a softening and soothing preparation, such as a decoction of hellebore and fenugreek and honey-sweetened clover in water, and it should be gentle;
puis soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos, et mette on desoz l’assele un sto de lainne igal, ne trop mol ne trop dur, puis mette li mires son talon sus le sto, et lieve le chief de l’espaule vertuousement, et traie la main dou malaide;	then have the patient lie on their back, and place a pad of equal thickness under the shoulder, not too soft nor too hard, then place the heel of the hand under the patient's armpit, and lift the affected shoulder gently, and pull the patient’s arm;
et uns autres ministres teigne lou chief dou malaide, si qu’il ne se mueve aval;	and another helper should hold the head of the patient so that it does not move downward;
celle espaule revient tout maintenant, et se tu vues si le ramoinne selonc ceste maniere:	the shoulder now returns completely, and if you wish to reset it according to this method:
et est que tu faices estre present I home qui soit plus grans que li malaides;	and it is that you have a man present who is larger than the patient;
et soit drois devers lou costeit, et boute s’espaule desoz l’assele dou malaide, et lieve l’assele en haut, si que li malaides pende en l’ar;	and let him stand facing the patient's side, and place his shoulder under the armpit of the patient, and lift the arm up so that the patient hangs in the air;
et uns autres ministres traie la main dou malaide aval devers lou ventre.	and another attendant pulls the patient's hand down towards the belly.
Et se li malaides est trop legiers, si pent avec lui aucune chose pesant, et li dislocation revient maintenant.	And if the patient is too light, he may hold something heavy with him, and the dislocation returns now.
Et le ramoinne on ausi en autre maniere:	And it is also reset in another manner:
et est c’on fiche I lonc tison en terre, dont li chiés soit ausi reons com I pistal, et ne soit ne trop gros ne trop graile;	and it is that you plant a long stick in the ground, which should be as thick as a pestle, neither too large nor too thin;
puis soit mis desoz lou malaide, mais k’il ait drapelz souef sus, et li malaides soit estans dou lonc dou fust;	then place it under the patient, but make sure there is cloth underneath, and the patient stands on top of the stick;
puis soit estendue sa main aval d’autre part forment, et li jointure revenra en son leu hastanment;	Then extend his hand from the other side, and the joint will return to its place quickly;
et s’elle ne vuet revenir por toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si fai ceste cure:	and if it does not want to return despite all the things we have said, then do this treatment:
pren I tison de II bras de grant et IIII dois de large, qui ait le chief reont por mues entrer em parfont desoz l’assele, selonc ceste forme:	take an iron rod that is two palms in length and four fingers wide, with a rounded head to easily enter under the skin, according to this form:
puis lie sus le chief dou fust drapelz souez, que li fust ne blece lou malaide, puis le met desoz l’assele dou malaide;	then wrap the head of the rod with a piece of cloth so that it does not hurt the patient, then place it under the skin of the patient;
et estende som bras sus le fust dou lonc, et lie l’ajutoire sus le fust, et lou bras au chief de la main, puis met le bras sus I eschillon d’une eschiele dou large, et soit estendue li mains aval, et soit laissiez li cors pendans d’autre part:	and extend the arm over the long rod, and secure the shoulder on the rod, and the hand at the head of the rod, then place the arm on a board of suitable width, and extend the hand downward, and let the body hang from the other side:
li jointure reva ens maintenant.	The joint now returns to its place.
Et quant elle est ens, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient que tu mettes desoz l’assele une spere de laine igal, puis met l’emplaustre aparilliet de poudre dou molin, avec encens et aubun d’uef, sus toute l’espaule et entor, puis l’estrain desoz l’assele avenanment, et torne le liien sus l’emplaustre, et embraice la main a son col, et soit li mains demorans ensi.	And when it is in place, whatever the manner, you must put under the seat a sphere of even linen, then apply an ointment prepared with powdered miller's flour, with incense and egg albumen over the entire shoulder and around it, then stretch the patient gently from under the seat, and wrap the bandage over the ointment, and bind the hand to his neck, and let the hands remain thus.
Et covient qu’il menjuce poc, tant que li membres soit confortez, car il sanera plus tost;	And he should eat little until the limb is strengthened, for it will heal more quickly;
et puis menjuce plus aprés V jors ou VII, et le mueve;	and then eat more after five or seven days, and move it;
et s’il est fermeis et il n’est mollifiez, si est sanez.	and if it is hard and not softened, it is healthy.
Et se li jointure est fuer de leu por moistor que i est venue, ou por autre cause, si covient que tu i aministres cauteres a III pertus, si com il est mis devant ou chapistre des cauteres.	And if the joint is out of place due to moisture that has come into it, or for another reason, then you must administer cauterizations with three holes, as it is described before in the chapter on cauterizations.
Et se tu fais tout ceu, et il deslie aprés VII jors, et li jointure ne se tient, et ne puet lever som bras amont, adonc saiches que li nerf au chief de l’espaule sont copeit ou estendut ou amollis;	And if you do all this, and after seven days it still does not hold in place, and he cannot raise his arm, then know that the nerve at the top of the shoulder is cut or stretched or weakened;
et saiches que li jointure n’iert jamais fichie en son leu.	and know that the joint will never be fixed in its place.
Li dislocation qui est devers lou pis, et les mameles, ou derrier, si est faite par impulsion, et estendement de mains, et i aministre on autre lieure;	The dislocation towards the hip, and the breasts, or behind, is done by impulse, and extension of hands, and another minister is present there;
et cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and treat until he is healed.
Et se aprés la sanation vient grietez au membre, et tardemens em movement, si use li malaides bain maintes fois, tant que celle grietez soit alegie, et reviegne a sa premiere nature.	And if after recovery the member is stiff and slow in movement, the patient should take many baths until the stiffness is alleviated, and returns to its original state.
de la dislocation dou coute	of the dislocation of the elbow
Saiches que li jointure dou coute est desaluee a poinnes, et a poinnes revient;	Know that the joint of the elbow is dislocated by pins, and returns to place by pins;
et s’est desaluee de toutes pars, et meismement devant et derrier, et li dislocations n’est mie reponue, car on la voit bien et sent bien;	and if it is dislocated in all directions, especially front and back, and the dislocation is not hidden, for one can see it well and feel it well;
et desalue selonc chescune figure.	and dislocates according to each figure.
Et quant tu joins le coute malaide avec lou sain, si le pues veoir apertement.	And when you join the sick part with the healthy part, then you can see clearly.
Car li jointure est chevee, et ne puet ploier lou bras, ne touchier son espaule a tout.	For the joint is dislocated, and he cannot bend his arm nor touch his shoulder at all.
Et covient que tu le ramoinnes ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne, car se apostemes chaus i venoit, si seroit grief li ramener;	And it is necessary to reset it as abscesses may occur if not done properly, for if abscesses were to occur, it would be difficult to treat them;
et par aventure ne puet estre ramenez dou tout en tout, meismement quant ele est au derrier;	and by chance cannot be completely restored, especially when it is at the back;
si vaut pis que les autres dislocations, et est de plus grant dolor, et par aventure i vient li mors.	it is worse than other dislocations, and causes greater pain, and by chance leads to death.
Et li restauration si est, quant elle est telz c’on la puet ramener, que tu li estendes sa main a tes II mains;	And the restoration is such that when it can be returned to place, you extend their arm with both your hands;
et ses bras soit espandus, et les mains dou mire selonc le coute entor, desor et desoz, et boute la jointure a ses peuchas ensamble, ou a la racine de sa palme, tant qu’ele reviegne a son leu.	and their arms should be spread out, and the hands held by the healer around the side, from below and above, and push the joint with both palms together, or at the base of the palm, until it returns to its place.
Et se li dislocations est au devant, si revient quant il double sa main a sa main, et fier de la racine de la palme lou coute qui est desaluez.	And if the dislocation is at the front, it returns when he doubles his hand to his hand, and strikes from the root of the palm the knife which is dislodged.
Et s’il ne vuet revenir au leu, si aministre fort extension;	And if it does not return to its place, administer strong extension;
et est que dui ministre estendent le bras, et le teignent dui ministre, si qu’il ne se mueve a l’estension;	and it is that two ministers extend the arm, and they hold it steady by two ministers, so that it does not move during extension;
puis torne le bras de chescune part, puis que tu as envoloupeit un drapeil double lonc et large;	then turn the arm from each side, after you have wrapped it with a double layer of cloth long and wide;
et quant li mires a jointe la jointure a sa main, si l’oigne d’aucun oile por amolir la jointure, puis boute la jointure forment, tant qu’ele reviegne;	and when the physician joins the joint to the hand, he anoints it with some oil to soften the joint, then forcibly inserts the joint until it returns;
et quant elle est au leu, si met sus emplaustre sec avec aubun d’uef, et l’estrain forment, et pent le bras au col dou malaide, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le deslie.	and when it is in place, apply dry plasters with egg yolk on top, and bind it firmly, and tie the arm to the neck of the patient, and leave it for some days, then release it.
Et se li jointure est ferme en son leu, si deslie lou liien, et le laisse;	And if the joint is firmly in its place, loosen the ligament, and leave it;
et se tu vois que li jointure n’estrigne bien, si rencomence l’emplaustre et lou lien, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit fermement mis;	and if you see that the joint does not fit well, restart the plaster and the ligament, and leave it like this for some days, until it is firmly set;
puis le deslie.	then loosen it.
Et se il sent grieteit aprés le ramenement de la jointe, et elle se muet, si le baigne et frote bellement, et presse tant qu’il soit assouagiez;	And if it feels stiff after the joint is returned and it does not move, bathe and rub it well, and press until it is alleviated;
ou tu met sus la jointure une naige de mouton grasse, puis la laisse I jor et une nuit, puis l’oste, et lou fai entrer ou bain;	and place a piece of fat sheep’s wool on the joint, then leave it for one day and one night, then remove it, and have him enter the bath;
et quant il sue, se li frote la jointure tempreement, puis remet la naige sus, et puis entre ou bain;	and when it sweats, gently rub the joint, then put on the poultice, and then enter the bath;
et ensi fai II fois ou III, tant qu’il soit sanez;	and do this two or three times until he is healed;
et se tu vues, si met sus fien de vaiche moiste chaufeit avec burre, et l’estrain sus;	and if you wish, place moistened flax heated with butter upon it and apply it;
si revenra a sa disposition.	it will return to its proper position.
li dislocation de la main	the dislocation of the hand
Li jointure de la main desalue, et li revenue est legiere, plus que les autres jointures.	The dislocation of the finger joint and its reduction is easy, more so than other joints.
Toutevoie, il la covient ramener au leu hastanment, en l’oure meisme qu’ele est desaluee, ainsois que li leus soit enflez, ou qu’il i viegne aposteme chaut.	Nevertheless, it is necessary to return it to its place quickly, in the same hour that it becomes dislocated, before swelling occurs or an abscess forms.
Et li ramenemens si est que tu mettes la main malaide sus une tauble, et estende li ministres la main, et li mires la mette igal, ensi que il mette sa paume sus l’aparance de la jointure, et la boute tant qu’elle reviegne.	And the reduction is such that you place the affected hand on a table, and the assistant extends the hand, and the physician places it evenly, so that his palm lies over the appearance of the joint, and presses until it returns.
Toutevoie, il covient que vos regardez s’il est bien a leu;	Nevertheless, you must check if it is in place;
adonc mette li malaides lou dos de sa main sus une tauble a l’estension et au ramenement.	then have the patient place the back of his hand on a table for extension and reduction.
Et se li dislocations est au dos de la main, si mette li malaides son dos de sa main sus la tauble, et li mires mette sa main sus cele apparance de la jointure.	And if the dislocation is on the back of the hand, have the patient place the back of their hand on a table, and the physician places their hand over that area of the joint.
S’elle revient maintenant, c’est bien.	If it returns now, it is well.
Se ce non, si l’estrain d’emplaustres apaisans apostemes chaus, et lou laisse ensi sens rencomencier.	If not, then apply soothing plasters to the abscesses and leave it thus without repeating.
Et s’il ne le puet soffrir, et tu ne la pues mettre au leu aprés aucuns jors, si demore li jointure torte;	And if he cannot bear it, and you cannot put it back into place after some days, the joint remains misaligned;
et ne nuist niant au malaide fuer que tant que li mains est amoillie, et ne puet estraindre aucune chose a tout:	and does no harm to the patient except that the hand remains soft, and cannot grasp anything firmly:
adonc saiches que li nerf sont copez, ou li artere;	then you know that the nerves are severed, or the artery;
si n’i a autre engien fuer que d’estraindre par cautere delez le cas, et par aventure n’i vaut autre chose.	there is no other remedy except to cauterize near the wound, and perhaps nothing else is worth doing.
Et quant li mains est au leu, si met sus l’emplaustre que nos avons dit, puis l’estrain et le laisse V jors, puis le deslie et laisse ensi.	And when it is in place, apply the plaster we have mentioned, then press it and leave it for five days, then untie it and leave it thus.
Et s’il ne la puet bien movoir, et il i a aucune grieteit, si la moille d’aigue chaude, et le frote tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if he cannot move it well, and there is some stiffness, then moisten it with warm water, and rub it until it is healed.
de la dislocation des dois de la main	of the dislocation of the thumb of the hand
Aucune fois sont desaluez li doi de la main a chescune part, aucune fois au dos de la palme ou au ventre;	Sometimes the thumb of the hand is dislocated on each side, sometimes at the back of the palm or on the front.
adonques estent le doi, et boute la dislocation a tes pouchés tant qu’il reviegne, puis sostien lou chief dou doi, et le pent vers la partie ou il est desjoins;	Then straighten the shoulder, and push the dislocation towards where it needs to go, then support the head of the shoulder, and pull it toward the part where it is dislocated.
et le laisse II jors, et puis le met igal celui jor;	and leave it for two days, and then put it back in place that same day;
et de nut le lie, si com nos avons dit, et lou deslie de jor, et lou fai movoir, et le relie la nut;	and bind it as we have said, and loosen it during the day, and move it, and bind it again at night;
et fai ce sovent, tant qu’il soit estroit, et tout ausi fai, se il est desaluez au ventre de la main, et fai si com tu as fait ci devant, tant qu’il soit sanez;	and do this frequently, until it is stable, and do the same if it is dislocated at the palm of the hand, and do as you have done before, until it is healed;
et tout ausi fai, quant il est desaluez d’autre part.	and do the same when it is dislocated from another part.
dou desaluement de l’eschinee dou dos	of the dislocation of the backsplice
Quant l’eschinee dou dos ou dou col est desaluee, ou il en i a plusors desaluees, si n’i a point de cure, car li mors haste le malaide.	When the dislocation of the back or neck occurs, and there are many such dislocations, there is no remedy, for death swiftly overtakes the patient.
Et li signes si est que li egestions saut fuer sens volunteit, ne ne la puet tenir, et maintes fois sont mollifiez aucun membre, ou les II cuixes ou li dui bras ou I.	And the signs are that the patient vomits involuntarily, cannot hold it, and sometimes certain limbs become weakened, such as both legs or both arms or one.
Et maintes fois se muet li eschinee a IIII pars;	And the fracture often shifts into four parts;
celle qui se muet au derrier si est apelee «gilbositez»:	the one that moves backward is called "gilbositez":
li cure si est que tu rewarde se li gilbositez est venue d’enfance:	the treatment is to check if the gilbositez came from childhood:
si n’i ait point de cure ne de sanation dou tot.	then there is no cure or healing for it.
Et celle que vient de cheoir ou de percussions ou de semblans choses, dirent li ancien manieres de cures par grans paroles, ou il n’a mie en toutes grant profit;	And the one that comes from falling or blows or similar things, the ancient methods of treatment speak in great words, but they are of no great benefit in all cases;
mais je l’ai abregiet selonc mon entention, et ai formez estrumens en diverses manieres.	but I have shortened it according to my intention, and have fashioned instruments in various manners.
Je dis que en la gilbositeit que vient au pis devant, nen a engien ne santeit;	I say that in the swelling that comes to the foot's front part, there is neither remedy nor health;
et ausi cele que vient droitement en II costez, et ne puet on curer fuers que celi proprement qui vient au dos, si com je dis;	and also the one that comes directly to two sides, and cannot be treated except by the one who treats it properly for the back, as I say;
et est que li malaides soit estendus sus sa faice en I leu igal, et ait de l’estrain desoz lui, qu’il ne se blece;	and it is that the patient lie stretched on his back in an equal place, and have someone behind him to support him so he does not injure himself;
puis fiche I tison au chief en terre forment, et I autre as piez, et lie un liien pardesoz les asseles dou malaide, et I autre as hainches, et as genous, et as chevilles;	then place a torch at the head in the ground firmly, and one at the feet, and tie a rope under the buttocks of the patient, and another at the hips, and at the knees, and at the ankles;
et dui ministre saichent les liiens, li uns au chief et li autres as piez, parmi les II tisons;	And two ministers hold the ropes, one at the head and the other at the feet, between the two torches;
et soient bien fermez, li tison si com nos avons dit, et li mires mette ses paumes sus l’espinee forment, tant qu’ele reviegne.	And let them be well secured, the torch as we have said, and the physician place his palms on either side of the spine, until it comes back into alignment.
Et s’elle ne revient par ceste cure, si pren une tauble de III bras de lonc, et chevé desoz la paroit, et li malaides soit en costé, et boute le chief de la tauble desoz la paroit, puis met le mileu de la tauble sus l’espinee;	And if it does not return with this treatment, take a board three arms long and place it under the wall, and have the patient lie on their side, then put the end of the board under the wall, then place the middle of the board over the spine;
et mette li mires ses piez sus l’autre chief de la tauble, et presse bien, tant qu’il reviegne au leu;	and have the physician place his feet on the other end of the board, and press firmly until it comes back into place;
et se tu vues, si le fai au tornet qui torne a la main.	and if you wish, do it with the twist that turns to the hand.
Et est que tu fiches II tisons au chief dou malaide d’un bras de grant, et devers les piez II autres, et ait entre chescun tison, desoure et desoz, une paume d’espaice de lonc;	And it is that you fix two torches at the head of the patient on one large arm, and near the feet two others, and there should be between each torch, above and below, a palm's space in length;
et ait en chescun tison I pertus, ou li tornet corre, et soient li tison fermement en terre, si qu’il ne se muevent;	and in each torch there should be one hole through which the twist runs, and the torches should be firmly fixed in the ground so that they do not move;
et entre chescuns II tisons ait I tison tornant, sor coi li liien tornent, et ait en II tornans II petis tisons d’une paume de lonc, por torner le tornet;	and between each pair of torches there should be one rotating torch, on which the ropes rotate, and there should be two small torches of a palm's length in both rotating ones, to twist the rope;
et puis lie lou lien qui est parmi les asseles au tornet devers le chief, et l’autre liien devers les piez a l’autre tornet, et chescuns des ministres torne son tornet a tout le liien, et li maistres mette l’espinee igal si com nos avons dit.	And then tie the bandage that is between the rollers near the head, and the other bandage near the feet to the other roller, and each of the assistants turns their roller on both sides of the bandage, and the master places the splint evenly as we have said.
Et quant elle est igalz, si met sus emplaustre desiccatif avec abun d’uef, et puis les estoupes, et puis l’estele d’une tablete de III dois de lonc, que porpreigne lou leu de la gilbositeit et la partie de l’espondile sainne, puis le lie d’un liien, si com nos avons dit, et use li malaides de norrissement subtil, tant qu’il soit sanez;	And when it is even, apply a desiccative plaster with an abundance of egg, and then the bandages, and then a stick from a tablet three digits long to mark the location of the gibbosity and the healthy part of the spine, then tie it with a bandage as we have said, and let the patient use subtle nourishment until he is well.
