et s’aucune chose vient en la fin de la santez, si covient aministrer medicines amollissans et asouajans, avec l’estele que nos avons dit ci devant;	And if anything comes up at the end of the healing process, it is necessary to administer softening and soothing medications, along with the stick we mentioned previously.
et aucune fois i aministre on une piece de plonc, et aucune fois vient li apparance en la derriere spondile dou dos, et cuide on que ce soit dislocations;	And sometimes a piece of bone is administered, and sometimes the appearance comes in the last vertebra of the back, and one thinks it is a dislocation;
et c’est li os qui apert, por coi on n’i doit mie avoir presumption:	And this is the bone that appears, for which one must not have false assumptions:
par aventure feroit venir la mort.	it might accidentally bring about death.
des dislocations de la hainche	Dislocations of the hip
Saiches que as jointures de la hainche et as jointures de l’espaule ne vient fuers que dislocacions soulement, ne n’i vient mie si com as autres jointures;	Know that at the joints of the hip and the shoulders only dislocations occur, not like other joints;
et li jointure de la hainche est desaluee selonc IIII parties:	and the joint of the hip is dislocated according to four parts:
dedens et defuer ,et devant et derrier;	inside and outside, and in front and behind;
et plus dedens c’aillors, et poc desalue devant et derrier.	and deeper within there, and a little dislocated before and behind.
Et li conoissance de sa dislocations dedens si est que quant on joint la jambe malaide avec la sainne, si est plus longe, et apert plus li malaides genous que li sains, et ne puet li malaides doubler son genoil au feu;	And the knowledge of this dislocation inside is such that when you join the sick leg with the healthy one, it is longer, and the patient's knee appears more prominent than the healthy one, and the patient cannot bend their knee at all.
et est li leus qui est delez enflez d’aposteme chaut, por ceu que li chiés de la cuixe vient lai.	and the area near which is swollen with an abscess is hot, because the thigh bone extends there.
Et li signe de celui cui il vient au defuer, si est que cist accident sont contraire a ces devant.	And the signs of him who is coming to faint are contrary to those before.
Et li signes de celui cui avient au devant, si est qu’il estent bien sa jambe selonc l’acomplissement;	And the signs of one who is affected in front are that they stretch their leg according to the extent of the injury;
toutevoie, ne double mie le genoil sens dolor, et s’on le vuet faire aler, si ne puet avant, et retient son urine, et enfle li angre, et quant il vait, si passe sus le talon.	nevertheless, they cannot bend the knee without pain, and if one wants to make them move forward, they cannot go ahead, and they hold their urine, and their ankle swells, and when they walk, they step over the heel.
Et li signes de celui cui il avient derrier, si est qu’il ne puet espandre son genoil, ne doubler, et est celle jambe plus torte de l’autre, et li angre est mollifié, et est li chiés de la cuixe au leu desoz les costes.	And the signs of him who is about to be dislocated behind are that he cannot extend his knee or bend it, and that leg is more crooked than the other, and the joint is softened, and the head of the thigh is in a position below the ribs.
Li ramenemens de ceste semblance de dislocation si est que tu rewarde se li dislocations est anciainne, et elle demore selonc sa disposition, si n’i a nule cure;	The remedy for this type of dislocation is that you observe whether the dislocation is old, and it remains according to its condition, if there is no treatment;
et n’i covient mie qu’il ait presumption.	and it is not appropriate for it to be treated with presumption.
Et en celi dont li dislocation est fresche, et c’est des IIII manieres de dislocation, si te haste que tu tornes la jointe, et l’esten dedens et defuer, et la muef a destre et senestre;	And in the case where the dislocation is fresh, and this is one of the four types of dislocations, hurry to return the joint, and stretch it inward and outward, and move it side to side;
par aventure si revenra, et n’a mestier d’autre cure.	perhaps it will return, and no other treatment is necessary.
Et s’il ne revient en ceste maniere, si covient que tu apareilles I ministre fort, et esten la jambe fort a II mains, ou a I liien que soit liiez sus lou genoil;	And if it does not return in this manner, then you must prepare a strong assistant, and stretch the leg strongly with two hands, or use a strap tied above the knee;
et uns autres ministres estende sa main desus en teil maniere qu’il boute ses mains desoz ses asseles, puis l’estrigne d’un souef liien sus la cuixe;	And another minister extends his hand above in such a way that he places his hands below the knees, then tightens them with a single swift bandage around the thigh;
et uns autres tigne lou chief dou liien;	And another holds the head of the bandage;
et estendent amont et aval tuit a une fois, tant que li malaide soit levez de terre a une fois, et demoure pendans.	and they extend upwards and downwards all at once, so that the patient is lifted off the ground at once, and remains suspended.
Ceste maniere d’estension si est commune as IIII semblances, et se li dislocation est revenue, si com nos avons dit, c’est bien.	This method of extension is common to the four similar cases, and if the dislocation has returned, as we have said, it is correct.
Se ceu non, si covient mettre cure a sa semblance.	If not, then it is necessary to apply treatment as appropriate.
Quant li dislocations est au pardedens, si covient que tu sovines le malaide sus son costeit sain, puis met le liien sus la racine de la cuixe, et le leu qui est desoz l’angre, puis estent le liien en haut devers l’angre, et devers la forcele;	When the dislocation is inward, you must place the patient on their healthy side, then apply the bandage at the root of the thigh, and below the armpit, then extend the bandage upwards towards the armpit, and towards the shoulder;
puis preigne uns autres ministres ses bras, et embraice le gros leu de la cuixe malaide, et l’estende au defuer forment:	Then take another assistant his arms, and embrace the thick part of the diseased thigh, and stretch it out forcefully:
si revenra a son leu maintenant;	it will return to its place now;
et ceste maniere de dislocation est plus legiere des autres.	and this method of reduction is less severe than the others.
Et se tu ne la pues serrer en ceste maniere que nos avons dit, si covient que tu lies les II piés dou malaide ensamble d’un fort liien souef sus les II talons, et sus les II genous, et soit li jambe malaide estendue II dois plus que li autres;	And if you cannot secure it in the manner we have described, then you must bind the two feet of the patient together with a strong bandage beneath the two heels and above the two knees, and let the affected leg be extended two thumbs' width more than the other;
puis soit pendus sus le chief d’un fust, et soit en sus de terre II bras de lonc;	then suspend him from above his head on a post, and let it be two arms' length off the ground;
puis comande a I ministre qu’il embraice le chief de la cuixe, et soit uns autres ministres pendans avec le malaide, qui embraice forment la cuixe, car li jointure revient maintenant hastanment.	Then instruct the minister to embrace the head of the thigh, and let another minister hang with the patient, who firmly embraces the thigh, because the joint now returns quickly.
Et quant li dislocations est au defuer, si gise li malaides, si com nos avons dit en celui qui a gilbositeit, et estraigne I liien sus la jambe malaide proprement, et sus le peis ausi;	And when the dislocation is out of place, let the patient lie down as we have said for one who has gout, and tightly bind the limb on the affected leg, and do the same on both sides;
puis met II tisons, I au chief et I autre as piez, puis fiche I tison entre les cuixes au malaide emmi la forme;	then place two torches, one at the head and one at the feet, then insert a torch between the thighs of the patient in the proper position;
et ait plantei de drapelz moistes entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide, puis estende chescuns ministre devers lui, et li mires mette igal a sa main la dislocation.	and let there be placed wet cloths around it so that it does not burn the patient, then extend each minister toward him, and the doctor places his hand equally on the dislocation.
S’elle revient, c’est boin.	If it returns, it is good.
Se ce non, met sus .ie. table, et le presse ensi com nos avons dit en la gilbositeit, et gise li malaides sus le sain costeit.	If not, place him on the table and press as we have said for gout, and let the patient lie on the healthy side.
Et quant li dislocations est devant, si covient estendre la jambe malaide hastanment, et selonc ce que j’ai dit;	And when a dislocation is present, it is necessary to extend the affected leg quickly, as I have said;
et mette li mires sa paine d’estre sus l’angre malaide, puis presse a l’autre main, et l’estent aval devers lou genoil.	and place your hand on the affected side, then press with the other hand, and extend it downward toward the knee.
Et se li dislocations est au defuer, si ne covient pas estendre le malaide aval, ne lever sus la terre, ains covient qu’il soit ausi com se li hainche estoit desaluee au defuer, si com nos avons dit dou couchement sus les II hainches;	And if the dislocation is behind, it should not be extended downward, nor lifted up from the ground, but rather it should be as if the hip were dislocated to the rear, as we have described for lying on both hips;
et soit sus sa faice, et li lien estendut si com nos avons dit ci devant, et doit om presser sus la jointure a la table;	and let him lie on his back, and the limb should be extended as we said before, and one must press upon the joint toward the table;
et sera a point quant li malaides estendra ses jambes, et elles seront igalz;	and it will be proper when the patient extends his legs, and they will be even;
adonques ajoste les cuixes, et met l’emplaustre, et l’estrain d’un bendeil, si que li hainche ne se mueve;	then apply the poultice, and bind it tightly with a bandage so that the thigh does not move;
et se repose III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie, et met l’emplaustre sus;	and let him rest for three or four days, then loosen it, and apply the poultice again;
et se tu vois qu’elles soient igalz, si l’estrain, si com devant, et le laisse III jors;	and if you see that they are even, bind them as before, and leave it for three days;
puis le deslie, et lou fai aler belement, tant que li membres soit confortez.	then loosen it, and have him walk gently, until the limb is comfortable.
de la dislocation dou genoil	Of the dislocation of the knee
Li genous est desaluez selonc III manieres:	The knee is dislocated in three ways:
c’est a savoir, dedens et defuer, et derrier;	that is to say, inside and outward, and behind;
et ne desalue point devant.	and do not reset it in front.
Et li signes si est que tu comande au malaide qu’il plie sa jambe a sa cuixe, et s’ele ne s’aert a sa cuixe, saiches qu’il est desaluez;	And the sign is that you instruct the patient to bend his leg at the thigh, and if it does not hold at the thigh, then you know it is dislocated;
et li restauration de toutes si est que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et estende sa jambe s’il puet, et li met ton dos sus sa faice, et met son piet sus tes piez;	and the restoration of all is that you have the patient sit upright, and extend his leg if he can, and place your back against his chest, and put his foot on your feet;
puis pren son genoil a tes paumes, et retrai entre tes dois, puis plie les II costez dou genoil forment;	then take his knee in your palms, and pull between your hands, then bend the two sides of the knee firmly;
et uns autres ministres estende son piet, tant que li genous reviegne a son leu, et li signes est qu’il aert bien sa jambe a sa cuixe legierement;	and another minister extends his foot so that the knee returns to its place, and the sign is that he holds his calf to his thigh lightly;
et met l’emplastre sus, et fai aerdre la jambe a la cuixe, et les loie ensamble fort III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie;	and place the plaster on it, and bind the leg to the thigh tightly for three or four days, then unbind it;
et ne se travaille mie li malaides d’aler, tant que li membres soit confortez.	and the patient does not work to walk until the limb is strengthened.
Et se li membres n’est a point, si aministre estendement fort, si com nos avons dit en la cure de la hainche, tant qu’il soit sanez	And if the limb is not properly aligned, apply strong extension, as we have said in the treatment of the thigh, until it is healthy
de la dislocation dou talon	of the dislocation of the heel
Li talons est aucune fois esmeus, et aucune fois desaluez plenement, et dedens et defuer.	The heels are sometimes bruised, and sometimes completely dislocated, both inward and outward.
Et li signes si est que li cheville est enflee, et tent avant a la partie ou elle est desaluee:	And the sign is that the ankle is swollen, and feels loose at the part where it is dislocated:
li ramenemens si est legier, et le doit on estendre legierement a ses mains quant il est esmeus soulement.	the reduction is light, and it should be extended gently with his hands when he is only slightly awake.
Et quant il est desaluez dou tot, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et le tigne I ministres fors par la jambe, desus la cheville;	And when it is dislocated immediately, you should seat the patient upright, and have one minister hold his leg out above the ankle;
puis trai le piet a toi a ta main destre, et puis a la senestre II fois, puis l’estent en haut, et boute bellement lou piet en haut;	then pull the foot towards you with your right hand, and then twice with your left hand, then extend it upwards, and forcefully push the foot upward;
et fai ce II fois, si com nos avons dit, em boutant et en traiant lou piet;	and do this twice as we have said, pushing and pulling the foot;
s’elle revient, c’est bien;	if it returns, that is good;
se ce non, si rencomence l’ovraige, car il revient;	if not, then restart the work, for it will return;
et s’il ne puet revenir ensi, si fai gesir lou malaide sor son dos sus terre, et fiche I passeil fermement en terre entre ses cuixes, et lie drapelz entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide;	and if it cannot return in this way, then have the patient lie down on his back on the ground, and firmly fix a lever in the ground between his thighs, and tie ropes around him so that he does not move;
puis teigne li ministres la cuixe, et uns autres ministres estende lou piet a ses mains ou a I liien, k’il lie sus le col dou piet;	Then the ministers should hold the thigh, and another minister should extend the foot with his hands or to the post, where he binds it at the neck of the foot;
puis estende chescuns ministres igalment, et li passelz soit adés entre les cuixes dou malaide por retenir le malaide quant on l’estent;	Then each minister should extend equally, and the patient should be firmly between the thighs of the ministers to hold the patient when they stretch him;
puis mette li mires igal la dislocation a ses mains, et uns autres ministres teigne la jambe sainne au desoz, et li dislocation revenra hastanment.	Then the physician should place the dislocation in his hands equally, and another minister should hold the healthy leg from behind, and the dislocation will quickly return to its proper position.
Et quant elle iert a point, si met l’emplastre et estoupes sus, et l’estrain forment, et lie lou piet a la jambe, et warde les ners qui sont sus la cheville derrier, que li liiens ne soit trop estrois;	And when it is properly set, apply the plaster and bandages firmly, and bind the foot to the leg, and guard the nerves that are behind the ankle, so that the bandage is not too tight;
puis le laisse II jors ou III, et se li liiens amolist, si l’estrain;	then leave it for two days or three, and if the ligaments soften, then hold it;
puis le deslie au tier jor ou au quart, et deffent a aler lou malaide par IIII jors;	then unbind it on the third day or fourth, and forbid the patient from walking for four days;
et s’il va devant cel termine, ce n’est mie seurtez qu’il ne desalue encor.	and if he walks before this期限，他就不会再次脱位吗？似乎这句话的翻译中出现了一个理解上的偏差，正确的翻译应该是：
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si covient que tu l’apaises, si com nos avons dit autre part, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if painful abscesses come, you must calm them as we have said elsewhere, until they are healed.
des dois	of the two
Quant li doi sont desaluez, si les covient bellement estendre sens travail, et c’est legiere chose.	When both are dislocated, they must be gently extended without strain, and this is an easy task.
Et se li dislocations est en aucun nout dou dos dou piet, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide sus I leu plain ou sus .ie. table tot droit, et met ton piet sus ce qui apert de ces jointures, puis presse a ton piet forment, tant qu’il reviegne;	And if the dislocation is in any part of the back of the foot, then you must have the patient sit on a flat place or on .ie. a straight table, and put your foot over what appears to be the joints, then press strongly with your foot until it returns;
et quant il est igalz, et il n’i apert nient, si met desoz la plante dou piet une table a II chiés, puis l’estrain forment, et le laisse III jors, puis le deslie;	and when it is even and nothing appears, place under the sole of the foot a board with II joints, then press firmly, and leave it for III days, then release;
et le fai reposer, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and have him rest until he is healed.
de plaie et de dislocation ensamble	of wound and of dislocation together
Quant plaie vient avec la dislocation, et on la vuet restorer, maintes fois avient que li malaides muert:	When a wound comes with the dislocation, and one wishes to restore it, many times the patient dies:
si ne soies mie presumptuous en la cure, se tu n’es saiges en l’art et tu ne l’as useit longement, et se tu n’es pitous et misericors et tardis, ne mie hardis;	Do not be presumptuous in the treatment if you are not wise in the art and have not used it for a long time, and if you are not compassionate and cautious, but rather bold;
et use au comencement de choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et laisse le malaide en la main Deu, se tu n’i vois esperance de santeit;	and at the beginning of treating hot abscesses, use soothing methods, and leave the patient in God's hands if you see no hope for recovery;
et quant tu i vois esperance, si ramoinne maintenant le membre au leu, ainsois que li apostemes chaus i viegne;	and when you see hope for recovery, then reset the limb to its place so that the hot abscesses can come forth;
et quant li membres est a leu, si aministre choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et cure la plaie, si com il covient, d’oignemens desiccatis;	and when the limb is in place, administer soothing treatments for hot abscesses, and treat the wound as necessary with drying ointments;
et se avec la dislocation a brisure, et os menus desevrez, si les oste, et fai ce que nos avons dit en maladies simples;	And if with the dislocation there is a fracture, and small bones displaced, remove them, and do as we have said in simple diseases;
et te garde d’entrer en voie de paour, selonc ce que j’ai dit, car ce te vaut mues selonc ton Creator, et por la saveteit de t’arme et de ton cors.	And guard against entering the path of fear as I have said, for it leads you according to your Creator's will, and for the skill of your arm and body.
